10142-8{_}741{_}"Oh, Philip, I am sure it can only be a joke," Mrs. Maxa replied.
10142-8{_}742{_}"I should love to know what you meant when you spoke of the children of Wallerstätten."
10142-8{_}743{_}"It happens to be one and the same thing," the brother replied.
10142-8{_}744{_}"Come here now and sit down beside me and get your mending-basket right away so that you won't have to jump up again.
10142-8{_}745{_}I know you.
10142-8{_}746{_}You will probably run off two or three times to the children."
10142-8{_}747{_}"No, Philip, to-day is Sunday and I won't mend.
10142-8{_}748{_}The children are all sleeping peacefully, so please tell me about it."
10142-8{_}749{_}Uncle Philip sat down quietly beside his sister and began: "As surely as I am now sitting here beside you, Maxa, so surely young Leonore of Wallerstätten was sitting beside me three days ago.
10142-8{_}750{_}I am really as sure as anything that it was Leonore's child.
10142-8{_}751{_}She is only an hour's distance away from you and is probably going to stay in this neighborhood for a few weeks.
10142-8{_}752{_}I wanted to bring you this news as a present."
10142-8{_}753{_}Mrs. Maxa first could not say a word from astonishment.
10142-8{_}754{_}"Are you quite sure, Philip?"
10142-8{_}755{_}she asked, wishing for an affirmation.
10142-8{_}756{_}"How could you become so sure that the child you saw was Leonore's little daughter?"
10142-8{_}757{_}"First of all, because nobody who has known Leonore can ever forget what she looked like.
10142-8{_}758{_}The child is exactly like her and looks at one just the way Leonore used to do.
10142-8{_}759{_}Secondly, the child's name was Leonore, too.
10142-8{_}760{_}Thirdly, she had the same brown curls rippling down her shoulders that her mother had, and she spoke with a voice as soft and charming.
10142-8{_}761{_}For the fifth and sixth reasons, because only Leonore could have such a child, for there could not be two people like her in the whole world."
10142-8{_}762{_}Uncle Philip had grown very warm during these ardent proofs.
10142-8{_}763{_}"Please tell me exactly where and how you saw the child," the sister urged.
10142-8{_}764{_}So the brother related how he had come back three days ago from a trip and, arriving in town, had given orders in the hotel for a carriage to be brought round to take him back to Sils that same evening.
10142-8{_}765{_}The host had then informed him that two ladies had just ordered a carriage to take them to the same destination.
10142-8{_}766{_}He thought that as long as they had seemed to be strangers and were anxious to know more about the road, they would be very glad to have a companion who was going the same way.
10142-8{_}767{_}So the host had made all necessary arrangements, as there were no objections to the plan on either side.
10142-8{_}768{_}When the carriage had driven up, he had seen that the ladies had with them a little daughter who was to occupy the back-seat of the carriage.
10142-8{_}769{_}"This daughter, as I thought, was Leonore's child.
10142-8{_}770{_}I am as certain of that as of my relation with you," the brother concluded.
10142-8{_}771{_}Mrs. Maxa was filled with great excitement.
10142-8{_}772{_}Could one of the children for whom she had vainly longed and inquired for such long years be really so near her?
10142-8{_}773{_}Would she be able to see her?
10142-8{_}774{_}Who were the ladies to whom she belonged?
10142-8{_}775{_}To all her various questions the brother could only answer that the ladies with whom Leonore was living came from the neighborhood of Hannover.
10142-8{_}776{_}They had taken a little villa in Sils on the mountain, which they had seen advertised for the summer months.
10142-8{_}777{_}He had shown the ladies his estate in Sils and had offered to serve them in whatever way they wished.
10142-8{_}778{_}Then they had taken leave.
10142-8{_}779{_}Leonore's name had wakened so many happy memories of her beautiful childhood and youth in Mrs. Maxa that she began to revive those times with her brother and tirelessly talked of the days they had spent there together with her unforgettable friend Leonore and her two cousins.
10142-8{_}780{_}The brother seemed just as ready to indulge in those delightful memories as she was, and whenever she ceased, he began again to talk of all the unusual happenings and exploits that had taken place with their dear friends.
10142-8{_}781{_}"Do you know, Maxa, I think we had much better playmates than your children have," he said finally.
10142-8{_}782{_}"If Bruno beats his comrades, I like it better than if he acted as they do."
10142-8{_}783{_}Brother and sister had not talked so far into the night for a long time.
10142-8{_}784{_}Nevertheless, Mrs. Maxa could not get to sleep for hours afterwards.
10142-8{_}785{_}Leonore's image with the long, brown curls and the winning expression in her eyes woke her lively desire to see the child that resembled her so much.
10142-8{_}786{_}CHAPTER III  CASTLE WILDENSTEIN  When Mäzli and Lippo were neatly washed and dressed the next morning, they came downstairs to the living-room chattering in the most lively manner.
10142-8{_}787{_}Mäzli was just telling Lippo her plans for the afternoon when he should be back from school.
10142-8{_}788{_}The mother, after attending to some task, followed the children, who were standing around the piano.
10142-8{_}789{_}As soon as she entered, Kurt broke out into a frightened cry.
10142-8{_}790{_}"Oh, mother, we have forgotten all about the poor people whose houses burnt down and we were supposed to take the things with us this morning."
10142-8{_}791{_}"Yes, the teacher told us twice that we must not forget it," Lippo complained, "but I didn't forget it."
10142-8{_}792{_}"Don't worry, children, I have attended to it," said the mother.
10142-8{_}793{_}"Kathy has just gone to the school with a basket full of things.
10142-8{_}794{_}It was too heavy for you to carry."
10142-8{_}795{_}"Oh, how nice and convenient it is to have a mother," Kurt said quite relieved.
10142-8{_}796{_}The mother sat down at the piano.
10142-8{_}797{_}"Come, let us sing our morning song, now," she said.
10142-8{_}798{_}"We can't wait for uncle, because he might come back too late from his walk."
10142-8{_}799{_}Opening the book, she began to sing "The golden sun--with joy and fun."
10142-8{_}800{_}The children taking up the melody sang it briskly, for they knew it well.
10142-8{_}801{_}Mäzli was singing full of zeal, too, and wherever she had forgotten the words, she did not stop, but made up some of her own.
10142-8{_}802{_}Two stanzas had been sung when Kurt said, "We must stop now or it will get too late.
10142-8{_}803{_}After breakfast it is time to go to school."
10142-8{_}804{_}The mother, assenting, rose and went to the table to fill their cups.
10142-8{_}805{_}But Lippo broke into a loud wail.
10142-8{_}806{_}Pulling his mother back, he cried, "Don't go!
10142-8{_}807{_}Please don't!
10142-8{_}808{_}We must finish it.
10142-8{_}809{_}We have to finish it.
10142-8{_}810{_}Come back, mother, come back."
10142-8{_}811{_}She tried to loosen the grip of the boy's firm little fingers on her dress and to calm him, but she did not succeed, and he kept on crying louder and louder: "Come back!
10142-8{_}812{_}You said one must not leave anything half done.
10142-8{_}813{_}We didn't finish the song and we must do it."
10142-8{_}814{_}Kurt now began to cry out, too: "Let go your pincher-claws--we'll get to school late."
10142-8{_}815{_}Mea's voice joined them with loud exclamation against Lippo, who was trying hard to pull his mother back, groaning loudly all the time.
10142-8{_}816{_}Uncle Philip entered at this moment.
10142-8{_}817{_}"What on earth is going on here?"
10142-8{_}818{_}he cried loudly into the confusion.
10142-8{_}819{_}Everybody began to explain.
10142-8{_}820{_}Lippo let go his grip at last and, approaching his uncle, solicited his help.
10142-8{_}821{_}Kurt's voice, however, was the loudest and he got the lead in telling about Lippo's obstinacy.
10142-8{_}822{_}"Lippo is right," the uncle decided.
10142-8{_}823{_}"One must finish what one has begun.
10142-8{_}824{_}This is a splendid principle and ought to be followed.
10142-8{_}825{_}Lippo has inherited this from his god-father and so he shall also have his help.
10142-8{_}826{_}Come Lippo, we'll sit down and finish the song to the last word."
10142-8{_}827{_}"But, Uncle Philip, the song has twelve stanzas, and we have to go to school.
10142-8{_}828{_}Lippo must go, too," Kurt cried out in great agitation.
10142-8{_}829{_}"He can't get an excuse for saying that he had to finish his morning song."
10142-8{_}830{_}"That is true, Kurt is right," said the uncle.
10142-8{_}831{_}"You see, Lippo, I know a way out.
10142-8{_}832{_}When you sing to-night, mother must promise me to finish the song.
10142-8{_}833{_}Then you will have sung it to the end."
10142-8{_}834{_}"We can't do that," Lippo wailed.
10142-8{_}835{_}"This is a morning song and we can't sing it at night.
10142-8{_}836{_}We must finish it now.
10142-8{_}837{_}Wait, Kurt!"
10142-8{_}838{_}he cried aloud, when he saw that the boy was taking up his school-bag.
10142-8{_}839{_}"What can we do?
10142-8{_}840{_}Where is your mother?
10142-8{_}841{_}Why does she run away at such a moment?"
10142-8{_}842{_}Uncle Philip cried out helplessly.
10142-8{_}843{_}"Call for your mother!
10142-8{_}844{_}You mustn't go on like that."
10142-8{_}845{_}Lippo had run back to the piano and, leaning against it, was crying bitterly.
10142-8{_}846{_}Kurt, after opening the door, called loudly for his mother in a voice that was meant to bring her from a distance.
10142-8{_}847{_}This exertion proved unnecessary, as she was standing immediately behind the door.
10142-8{_}848{_}Bruno, in order to question her about something, had drawn her out with him.
10142-8{_}849{_}"Oh, mother, come in!"
10142-8{_}850{_}Kurt cried in milder accents.
10142-8{_}851{_}"Come and teach our two-legged law-paragraph here to get some sense.
10142-8{_}852{_}School is going to start in five minutes."
10142-8{_}853{_}The mother entered.
10142-8{_}854{_}"Maxa, where did you go?"
10142-8{_}855{_}the brother accosted her.
10142-8{_}856{_}"It is high time to get this boy straightened out.
10142-8{_}857{_}Just look at the way he is clutching the piano in his trouble.
10142-8{_}858{_}He ought to be off.
10142-8{_}859{_}Kurt is right."
10142-8{_}860{_}The mother, sitting down on the piano-stool, took the little boy's hand and pulled him towards her.
10142-8{_}861{_}"Come, Lippo, there is nothing to cry about," she said calmly.
10142-8{_}862{_}"Listen while I explain this.
10142-8{_}863{_}It is a splendid thing to finish anything one has begun, but there are things that cannot be finished all at once.
10142-8{_}864{_}Then one divides these things into separate parts and finishes part first with the resolution to do another part the next day, and so on till it is done.
10142-8{_}865{_}We shall say now our song has twelve stanzas and we'll sing two of them every morning; in that way we can finish it on the sixth day and we have not left it unfinished at all.
10142-8{_}866{_}Can you understand, Lippo?
10142-8{_}867{_}Are you quiet now?"
10142-8{_}868{_}"Yes," said the little boy, looking up to his mother with an expression of perfect satisfaction.
10142-8{_}869{_}The leave-taking from the uncle had to be cut extremely short.
10142-8{_}870{_}"Come soon again," sounded three times more from the steps, and then the children started off.
10142-8{_}871{_}The mother, looking through the window, followed them with her eyes.
10142-8{_}872{_}She was afraid that Kurt and Mea would leave the little one far behind on account of having been kept too long already, and it happened as she feared.
10142-8{_}873{_}She saw Lippo trudging on behind with an extraordinarily full school-bag on his back.
10142-8{_}874{_}"Can you see what Lippo is carrying?"
10142-8{_}875{_}she asked her brother.
10142-8{_}876{_}The lid of the bag was thrust open and a thick unwieldy object which did not fit into it was protruding.
10142-8{_}877{_}"What is he carrying along, I wonder?
10142-8{_}878{_}Can you see what it is?"
10142-8{_}879{_}"I can only see a round object wrapped up in a gray paper," her brother replied.
10142-8{_}880{_}"I am sure it must be something harmless.
10142-8{_}881{_}I have to say that Lippo is a wonderfully obedient and good boy and full of the best sense.
10142-8{_}882{_}As soon as one says the right word to him, he comes 'round.
10142-8{_}883{_}Why did you wait so long though, Maxa, before saying it to him?"
10142-8{_}884{_}was Uncle Philip's rather reproachful question.
10142-8{_}885{_}"Why did you run away and leave him crying and moaning?
10142-8{_}886{_}He needed your help.
10142-8{_}887{_}What he wanted was perfectly correct but was not just suitable at that moment, and he needed an explanation.
10142-8{_}888{_}How could you calmly run away?"
10142-8{_}889{_}"It was just as necessary to hear Bruno's question," the sister said.
10142-8{_}890{_}"I knew that Lippo was in good hands.
10142-8{_}891{_}I thought naturally that you would be able to say the right word to him.
10142-8{_}892{_}You know yourself how he respects you."
10142-8{_}893{_}"Oh, yes, that is right," Uncle Philip admitted.
10142-8{_}894{_}"It is not always easy to say the right word to a little fellow who has the right on his side and needs to have the other side shown to him, too; he is terribly pedantic besides, and says that one can't sing a morning song in the evening, and when he began to wail in his helplessness, it made me miserable.
10142-8{_}895{_}How should one always just be able to say the right word?"
10142-8{_}896{_}His sister smiled.
10142-8{_}897{_}"Do you admit now, Philip, that bringing up children is not a very simple matter?"
10142-8{_}898{_}"There is a truth in what you say.
10142-8{_}899{_}On the other hand, it does not look very terrible, either," the brother said with a glance at Mäzli, who was quietly and peacefully sitting at the table, eating her bread and milk in the most orderly fashion.
10142-8{_}900{_}She had been compelled to stop in the middle of breakfast by the excitement caused by Lippo.
10142-8{_}901{_}It had been very thrilling, but now she could calmly finish.
10142-8{_}902{_}Uncle Philip suddenly discovered that the tune set for his departure was already past.
10142-8{_}903{_}Taking a rapid leave of his sister, he started to rush off, but she held him for a moment.
10142-8{_}904{_}"Please, Philip, try to find out for me about the little girl, to whom she belongs, and with whom she is travelling," she begged him eagerly.
10142-8{_}905{_}"Please do that for me!
10142-8{_}906{_}If your supposition, that she is Leonore's child is right, I simply must see her.
10142-8{_}907{_}Nobody can prevent me from seeing her once at least."
10142-8{_}908{_}"We'll see, we'll see," the brother answered hurriedly, and was gone the next moment.
10142-8{_}909{_}The day had started with so much agitation and it had all taken so much time that Mrs. Maxa had her hands full now in order to complete the most necessary tasks before the children came back from school.
10142-8{_}910{_}Mäzli was very obedient to-day and had settled down on her little chair.
10142-8{_}911{_}She was virtuously knitting on a white rag, which was to receive a bright red border and was destined to dust Uncle Philip's desk.
10142-8{_}912{_}It was to be presented to him on his next birthday as a great surprise.
10142-8{_}913{_}Mäzli had in her head this and many other thoughts caused by the morning's scene, so she did not feel the same inclination to set out on trips of discovery as usual, and remained quietly sitting on her chair.
10142-8{_}914{_}Her mother was extremely preoccupied, as could easily be seen.
10142-8{_}915{_}Her thoughts had nothing to do with either the laundry or the orders she was giving to Kathy, nor the cooking apples she had sorted out in the cellar.
10142-8{_}916{_}Her hand often lay immovably on these, while she absently looked in front of her.
10142-8{_}917{_}Her thoughts were up in the castle-garden with the lovely young Leonore, and in her imagination she was wandering about with her beloved friend, singing and chattering under the sounding pine trees.
10142-8{_}918{_}Her brother's news had wakened all these memories very vividly.
10142-8{_}919{_}Then again she would sigh deeply and another communication filled her full of anxiety.
10142-8{_}920{_}Bruno had asked her not to wait for him at dinner, as he had resolved to stop his comrades from a wicked design and therefore would surely be a trifle late.
10142-8{_}921{_}What this was and what action he meant to prevent the boy had not had time to say, for Kurt had opened the door at that moment calling for her with his voice of thunder.
10142-8{_}922{_}All she had been able to do was to beg Bruno, whatever happened, not to let his anger become his master.
10142-8{_}923{_}Sooner than the mother had expected Kurt's steps could be heard hurriedly running into the house followed by a loud call for her.
10142-8{_}924{_}"Here I am, Kurt," sounded calmly from the living-room, where his mother had finally settled down after her tasks, beside Mäzli's chair.
10142-8{_}925{_}"Come in first before you try to make your announcements; or is it so dreadfully urgent?"
10142-8{_}926{_}Kurt had already reached his mother's side.
10142-8{_}927{_}"Oh, mother, when I come home from school I'm never sure if you are in the top or the bottom of the house," he said, "so I have to inquire in plenty of time, especially when there is so much to tell you as there is to-day.
10142-8{_}928{_}Now listen.
10142-8{_}929{_}First of all, the teacher thanks you for the presents for the poor people.
10142-8{_}930{_}He lets you know that if you think it suitable to send them a helmet of cardboard with a red plume, he will put it by for the present.
10142-8{_}931{_}Or did you have a special intention with it?"
10142-8{_}932{_}"I do not understand a word of what you say, Kurt," the mother replied.
10142-8{_}933{_}That moment Lippo opened the door.
10142-8{_}934{_}He was apt to come home after the older boy, for Kurt was not obliged to wait for him after school.
10142-8{_}935{_}"Here comes the one who will be able to explain the precious gift you sent, mother," said Kurt.
10142-8{_}936{_}Lippo, trotting cheerfully into the room, had bright red cheeks from his walk.
10142-8{_}937{_}The mother began by asking, "Tell me, Lippo, did you take something to school this morning in your school-bag for the poor people whose houses were burnt?"
10142-8{_}938{_}"Yes, mother, my helmet from Uncle Philip," Lippo answered.
10142-8{_}939{_}"I see!
10142-8{_}940{_}You thought that if a poor little chap had no shirt, he would be glad to get a fine helmet with a plume for his head," Kurt said laughing.
10142-8{_}941{_}"You don't need to laugh!"
10142-8{_}942{_}Lippo said, a little hurt.
10142-8{_}943{_}"Mother told us that we must not only send things we don't want any more.
10142-8{_}944{_}So I gave the helmet away and I should have loved to keep it."
10142-8{_}945{_}"Don't laugh at him, Kurt; I really told him that," the mother affirmed.
10142-8{_}946{_}"He wanted to do right but he did not quite find the right way of doing it.
10142-8{_}947{_}If you had told me your intention, Lippo, I could have helped you to do some positive good.
10142-8{_}948{_}Next time you want to help, tell me about it, and we'll do it together."
10142-8{_}949{_}"Yes, I will," Lippo said, quite appeased.
10142-8{_}950{_}"Oh, mother, listen!"
10142-8{_}951{_}Kurt was continuing.
10142-8{_}952{_}"I have to tell you something you won't like and we don't like either.
10142-8{_}953{_}Just think!
10142-8{_}954{_}Loneli had to sit on the shame-bench to-day.
10142-8{_}955{_}But all the class is on Loneli's side."
10142-8{_}956{_}"But why, Kurt?
10142-8{_}957{_}The poor child!"
10142-8{_}958{_}the mother exclaimed.
10142-8{_}959{_}"What did she do?
10142-8{_}960{_}I am afraid that her honest old grandmother will take it terribly to heart.
10142-8{_}961{_}She'll be in deep sorrow about it and will probably punish Loneli again."
10142-8{_}962{_}"No, indeed, she must not do that," Kurt said eagerly.
10142-8{_}963{_}"The teacher said himself that he hated to put Loneli there, as she was a good and obedient child, but that he had to keep his word.
10142-8{_}964{_}He had announced that he was tired of the constant chattering going on in the school.
10142-8{_}965{_}To stop it he had threatened to put the first child on the shame-bench that was caught.
10142-8{_}966{_}So poor Loneli had to sit there all by herself and she cried so terribly that we all felt sorry.
10142-8{_}967{_}But of course, mother, a person doesn't talk alone, and Loneli should not have been obliged to stay there alone.
10142-8{_}968{_}The teacher had just asked: 'Who is talking over there?
10142-8{_}969{_}I can hear some whispering.
10142-8{_}970{_}Who is it?'
10142-8{_}971{_}Loneli answered 'I' in a low voice, so she had to be punished.
10142-8{_}972{_}One of her neighbors should have said 'I,' too, of course; it was perfectly evident that there was another one."
10142-8{_}973{_}"Loneli might have asked somebody a question which was not answered," his mother suggested.
10142-8{_}974{_}"Mea will know all about it, for she followed Loneli after school.
10142-8{_}975{_}Now more still, mother," Kurt continued.
10142-8{_}976{_}"Two boys from my class were beaten this morning by Mr. Trius.
10142-8{_}977{_}Early this morning they had climbed over the castle hedge to inspect the apples on the other side of the hedge.
10142-8{_}978{_}But Mr. Trius was already about and stood suddenly before them with his heavy stick.
10142-8{_}979{_}In a jiffy they had a real Trius-beating, for the hedge is high and firm and one can't get across it quickly.
10142-8{_}980{_}Now for my fourth piece of news.
10142-8{_}981{_}Farmer Max who lives behind the castle has told everybody that when his father came back late yesterday night from the cattle-fair in the valley, he saw a large coach, which was right behind his own, drive into the castle-garden.
10142-8{_}982{_}He was quite certain that it went there, but nobody seems to know who was in it.
10142-8{_}983{_}So you are really listening at last, mother!
10142-8{_}984{_}I noticed that you have been absentminded till now.
10142-8{_}985{_}Farmer Max told us something else about his father that you wouldn't like me to repeat, I know."
10142-8{_}986{_}"You would not say so if it were not wrong; you had better not repeat it, Kurt," said the mother.
10142-8{_}987{_}"No, indeed, it is not bad, but very strange.
10142-8{_}988{_}I can tell you though, because I don't believe it myself.
10142-8{_}989{_}Max told that his father said there was something wrong about the coach and that he went far out of its way.
10142-8{_}990{_}The coachman looked as if he only had half a head, and his coat-collar was rolled up terribly high in order to hide what was below.
10142-8{_}991{_}He was wildly beating the horses so that they fairly flew up the castle-hill, while sparks of fire were flying from their hoofs."
10142-8{_}992{_}"How can you tell such rubbish, Kurt?
10142-8{_}993{_}How should there be something unnatural in such a sight?"
10142-8{_}994{_}the mother scolded him.
10142-8{_}995{_}"I am sure you think that the Wildenstein ghost is wandering about again.
10142-8{_}996{_}You can see every day that horses' hoofs give out sparks when they strike stone, and to see a coachman with a rolled up collar in windy weather is not an unusual sight either.
10142-8{_}997{_}In spite of all I say to you, Kurt, you seem to do nothing but occupy yourself with this matter.
10142-8{_}998{_}Can't you let the foolish people talk without repeating it all the time?"
10142-8{_}999{_}Kurt was very glad when Mea entered at that moment, for he had really disobeyed his mother's repeated instructions in the matter.
10142-8{_}1000{_}But he comforted himself with the thought that he was only acting according to her ideas if he was finally able to prove to the people that the whole thing was a pure invention and could get rid of the whole thing for good.
10142-8{_}1001{_}"Why are your eyes all swollen?"
10142-8{_}1002{_}he accosted his sister.
10142-8{_}1003{_}Mea exploded now.
10142-8{_}1004{_}Half angry and half complaining, she still had to fight against her tears.

10142-8{_}1008{_}Then she always says I spoil the flowers on her hat because I shake them.
10142-8{_}1009{_}And then she turns her back on me and won't even speak to me."

10142-8{_}1015{_}All noise she thinks a great disgrace,     But tricks she does not lack.

10142-8{_}1021{_}There would be nothing to mourn over."
10142-8{_}1022{_}Mea, however, fought passionately for her friend and never gave way till Kurt had promised not to go on with his ditty.
10142-8{_}1023{_}But her mother wanted to know now what had given Mea such red eyes.

10142-8{_}1034{_}Kurt threw in.

10142-8{_}1058{_}The mother had put off preparations for dinner on purpose.

10142-8{_}1077{_}"The two told me last Saturday that they had a scheme for to-day in which I was to join.

10142-8{_}1117{_}Then queenie thinks: That's only fair,    She couldn't well refuse.

10142-8{_}1138{_}Soon everybody was merrily playing.

10142-8{_}1170{_}They all started and finished the whole song in peace.
10142-8{_}1171{_}When the mother came back later on from the beds of the two younger children, the three elder ones sat expectantly around the table, for Kurt had told them of their mother's promise to tell them the story of the family of Wallerstätten that evening.
10142-8{_}1172{_}They had already placed their mother's knitting-basket on the table in preparation of what was to come, because they knew that she would not tell them a story without knitting at the same time.
10142-8{_}1173{_}Smilingly the mother approached.
10142-8{_}1174{_}"Everything is ready, I see, so I can begin right away."
10142-8{_}1175{_}"Yes, and right from the start, please; from the place where the ghost first comes in."
10142-8{_}1176{_}The mother looked questioningly at Kurt.
10142-8{_}1177{_}"It seems to me, Kurt, that you still hope to find out about this ghost, whatever I may say to the contrary.
10142-8{_}1178{_}I shall tell you, though, how people first began to talk about a ghost in Wildenstein.
10142-8{_}1179{_}The origin of these rumors goes back many, many years."
10142-8{_}1180{_}"There is a picture in the castle," the mother began to relate, "which I often looked at as a child and which made a deep impression upon me.
10142-8{_}1181{_}It represents a pilgrim who wanders restlessly about far countries, despite his snow-white hair, which is blowing about his head, and despite his looking old and weather-beaten.
10142-8{_}1182{_}It is supposed to be the picture of the ancestor of the family of Wallerstätten.
10142-8{_}1183{_}The family name is thought to have been different at that time.
10142-8{_}1184{_}"This ancestor is said to have been a man extremely susceptible to violent outbreaks.
10142-8{_}1185{_}In his passion he was supposed to have committed many evil deeds, on account of which his poor wife could not console herself.
10142-8{_}1186{_}Praying for him, she lay whole days on her knees in the chapel.
10142-8{_}1187{_}She died suddenly, however, and this shocked the baron so mightily that he could not remain in the castle.
10142-8{_}1188{_}In order to find peace for his restless soul he became a repentant pilgrim.
10142-8{_}1189{_}So he took the emblem of a pilgrim into his coat of arms and called himself Wallerstätten.
10142-8{_}1190{_}Leaving his estate and his sons, he nevermore returned.
10142-8{_}1191{_}"Later on two of his descendants lived in the castle.
10142-8{_}1192{_}Both were well loved and respected, because they did a great deal to have the land cultivated for a long distance around and as a result all the farmers became rich.
10142-8{_}1193{_}But both had inherited the violent temper of their ancestor, and the truth is that there always were members in the family with that fatal characteristic.
10142-8{_}1194{_}Nobody knew what happened between the brothers, but one morning one of them was found dead on the floor of the big fencing-hall.
10142-8{_}1195{_}All that the castle guard knew about it was that his two masters had settled a dispute with a duel.
10142-8{_}1196{_}The other brother had immediately disappeared, but was brought back dead to the castle a few days afterwards.
10142-8{_}1197{_}"Climbing up a high mountain, he had fallen down a precipice and had been found dead.
10142-8{_}1198{_}These events threw all the neighborhood into great consternation.
10142-8{_}1199{_}"That is when the rumors first spread that the restless spirit of the brother murderer was seen wandering about the castle.
10142-8{_}1200{_}All this happened many years before my father and your grandfather moved into Nolla as Rector.
10142-8{_}1201{_}The rumor had somewhat faded then and all that we children heard about it was that my father was very positive in denying all such reports that reached his ears.
10142-8{_}1202{_}Your grandfather was the closest friend of the master of Wallerstätten, whom everybody called the Baron.
10142-8{_}1203{_}I can only remember seeing him once for a moment, but he made an unusual impression upon me.
10142-8{_}1204{_}I remember him very vividly as a very tall man going with rapid steps through the courtyard and mounting a horse, which was trying to rear.
10142-8{_}1205{_}He died before I was five years old, and I have often heard my father say to my mother that it was a great misfortune for the two sons to have lost their father.
10142-8{_}1206{_}I felt so sorry for them that I would often stop in the middle of play to ask her, 'Oh, mother, can nobody help them?'
10142-8{_}1207{_}To comfort me she would tell me that God alone could help.
10142-8{_}1208{_}For a long time I prayed every night before going to sleep: 'Dear God, please help them in their trouble!'
10142-8{_}1209{_}Both were always very kind and friendly with me.
10142-8{_}1210{_}I was up at the castle a great deal, because the Baroness Maximiliana of Wallerstätten was my godmother.
10142-8{_}1211{_}My father instructed the two sons and acted as helper and adviser to the Baroness in many things.
10142-8{_}1212{_}He went up to her every morning, holding me by one hand and Philip by the other.
10142-8{_}1213{_}My brother had lessons together with the boys, who were one year apart in age, while Philip was just between them.
10142-8{_}1214{_}Bruno, the elder--"  "I was named after him, mother, wasn't I?"

10142-8{_}1217{_}"You wanted a Salo so much and, as I was a girl, you called me Malomea, didn't you?"
10142-8{_}1218{_}The mother nodded.
10142-8{_}1219{_}"And I was called after father," Kurt cried out, in order to prove that his name also had a worthy origin.
10142-8{_}1220{_}"I went up to the castle because my godmother wished it.
10142-8{_}1221{_}She would have loved to have a little daughter herself, therefore she occupied herself with me as if I belonged to her.
10142-8{_}1222{_}She taught me to embroider and to do other fine handwork.
10142-8{_}1223{_}Whenever she went with me into the garden and through the estate, she taught me all about the trees and flowers.
10142-8{_}1224{_}I was often allowed to pick the violets that grew in great abundance beneath the hedges and in the grass at the border of the little woods.
10142-8{_}1225{_}Oh, what beautiful days those were!
10142-8{_}1226{_}Soon they were to become more perfect still for us.
10142-8{_}1227{_}"But I received an impression in those days which remained in my heart for a long while like a menacing power, often frightening me so that I was very unhappy.
10142-8{_}1228{_}Once my father came down very silently from the castle.

10142-8{_}1230{_}His mother is naturally more worried about this than about anything else.'"
10142-8{_}1231{_}"Look at him," Kurt said dryly, glancing at Bruno, who was sitting beside his mother.
10142-8{_}1232{_}For answer Bruno's eyes flashed threateningly at his brother.
10142-8{_}1233{_}"Oh, please go on, mother," Mea urged.
10142-8{_}1234{_}She was in no mood to have the tale interrupted by a fight between her brothers.
10142-8{_}1235{_}"It seemed terrible to me," the mother continued again, "that Bruno, my generous, kind friend, should have anything in his character to worry his mother.
10142-8{_}1236{_}Often I cried quietly in a corner about it and wondered how such a thing could be.
10142-8{_}1237{_}I had to admit it myself, however.
10142-8{_}1238{_}Whenever the three boys had a disagreement or anybody did something to displease Bruno, he would get quite beside himself with rage, acting in a way which he must have been sorry for later on.
10142-8{_}1239{_}I have to repeat again, though, that he had at bottom a noble and generous nature and would never have willingly harmed anyone or committed a cruel deed.
10142-8{_}1240{_}But one could see that his outbreaks of passion might drive him to desperate deeds.
10142-8{_}1241{_}"Salo, his brother, never became angry, but he had a very unyielding nature just the same.
10142-8{_}1242{_}He was just as obstinate in his way as his brother, and never gave in.
10142-8{_}1243{_}Philip was always on his side, for the two were the best of friends.
10142-8{_}1244{_}Bruno was much more reserved and taciturn than Salo, who was naturally very gay and could sing and laugh so that the halls would re-echo loudly with his merriment.
10142-8{_}1245{_}The Baroness herself often laughed in that way, too.
10142-8{_}1246{_}That is why Bruno imagined that she loved her younger son better than him, and because he himself loved his mother passionately, he could not endure this thought.
10142-8{_}1247{_}It was not true, however.
10142-8{_}1248{_}She loved his eldest boy passionately and everybody who was close to her could see it.
10142-8{_}1249{_}"When I was ten years old and Philip fifteen, an unusually charming girl was added to our little circle.
10142-8{_}1250{_}I above everybody else was enchanted with her.
10142-8{_}1251{_}Our friends at the castle and even Philip, who certainly was not easily filled with enthusiasm, were extremely enthusiastic about our new playmate.
10142-8{_}1252{_}She was a girl of eleven years old, you see just a year older than I was.
10142-8{_}1253{_}She was far, far above me, though, in knowledge, ability, and especially in her manners and whole behaviour, so that I was perfectly carried away by her charm.
10142-8{_}1254{_}"Her name was Leonore.
10142-8{_}1255{_}She was related to the baroness and had come down from the far north, in fact from Holstein, where my godmother came from and all her connections lived.
10142-8{_}1256{_}Leonore, the daughter of one of her relations, had very early lost her father and mother, as her mother had died soon after the Baroness decided to adopt the child.
10142-8{_}1257{_}She knew that Leonore would otherwise be all alone in the world, and she hoped that a gentle sister would have an extremely beneficial influence on the two self-willed brothers.
10142-8{_}1258{_}Now a time began for me which was more wonderful than anything I could ever have imagined.
10142-8{_}1259{_}Leonore was to continue her studies, of course, and take up new ones.
10142-8{_}1260{_}For that purpose a very refined German lady came to the castle very soon after Leonore's arrival.
10142-8{_}1261{_}Only years afterwards I realized what a splendid teacher she had been.
10142-8{_}1262{_}"My godmother had arranged for me to share the studies with Leonore, and therefore I was to live all day at the castle as her companion, only returning in the evenings.
10142-8{_}1263{_}So we two girls spent all our time together, and in bad weather I also remained there for the night.
10142-8{_}1264{_}Leonore had a tremendous influence on me, and I am glad to say an influence for my good, for I was able to look up to her in everything.
10142-8{_}1265{_}Whatever was common or low was absolutely foreign to her noble nature.
10142-8{_}1266{_}This close companionship with her was not only the greatest enjoyment of my young years, but was the greatest of benefits for my whole life."
10142-8{_}1267{_}"You certainly were lucky, mother," Mea exclaimed passionately.
10142-8{_}1268{_}"Yes, and Uncle Philip was lucky, too, to have two such nice friends," Bruno added.
10142-8{_}1269{_}"I realize that," the mother answered.
10142-8{_}1270{_}"You have no idea, children, how often I have wished that you, too, could have such friends."
10142-8{_}1271{_}"Please go on," Kurt begged impatiently.
10142-8{_}1272{_}"Where did they go, mother?
10142-8{_}1273{_}Doesn't anyone know what has become of them?"
10142-8{_}1274{_}"Whenever our brothers, as we called them, were free," the mother continued, "they were our beloved playmates.
10142-8{_}1275{_}We valued their stimulating company very much and were always happy when through some chance they were exempt from some of their numerous lessons.
10142-8{_}1276{_}They always asked us to join them in their games and we were very happy that they wanted our company.
10142-8{_}1277{_}Baroness von Wallerstätten had guessed right.
10142-8{_}1278{_}Since Leonore had come into our midst, the brothers fought much more seldom, and everybody who knew Bruno well could see that he tried to suppress his outbursts of rage in her presence.
10142-8{_}1279{_}Once Leonore had become pale with fright when she had been obliged to witness such a scene, and Bruno had not forgotten it.
10142-8{_}1280{_}Four years had passed for us in cloudless sunshine when a great change took place.
10142-8{_}1281{_}The young barons left the castle in order to attend a university in Germany, and Philip also left for an agricultural school.
10142-8{_}1282{_}So we only saw the brothers once a year, during their brief holidays in the summer.
10142-8{_}1283{_}Those days were great feast days then for all of us, and we enjoyed every single hour of their stay from early morning till late at night.
10142-8{_}1284{_}We always began and ended every day with music, and frequently whole days were spent in the enjoyment of it.
10142-8{_}1285{_}"Both young Wallerstättens were extremely musical and had splendid voices, and Leonore's exquisite singing stirred everybody deeply.
10142-8{_}1286{_}The Baroness always said that Leonore's voice brought the tears to her eyes, no matter if she sang merry or serious songs.
10142-8{_}1287{_}It affected me in that way, too, and one could never grow weary of hearing her.
10142-8{_}1288{_}I had just finished my seventeenth and Leonore her eighteenth year when a summer came which was to bring grave changes.
10142-8{_}1289{_}We did not expect Philip home for the holidays.
10142-8{_}1290{_}Through the Baroness' help he was already filling the post of manager of an estate in the far north.
10142-8{_}1291{_}The young barons had also completed their studies and were expected to come home and to consult with their mother about their plans for the future.
10142-8{_}1292{_}She fully expected them to travel before settling down, and after that she hoped sincerely that one of them would come to live at home with her; this would mean that he would take the care of the estate on his shoulders with its troubles and responsibilities.
10142-8{_}1293{_}Soon after their arrival the sons seemed to have had an interview with their mother which clearly worried her, for she went about silently, refusing to answer any questions.
10142-8{_}1294{_}Bruno strode up and down the terrace with flaming eyes whole hours at a time, without saying a word.
10142-8{_}1295{_}Salo was the only sociable one left, and sometimes he would come and sit down beside us; but if we questioned him about their apparent feud, he remained silent.
10142-8{_}1296{_}How different this was from our former gay days!
10142-8{_}1297{_}But this painful situation did not last long.
10142-8{_}1298{_}On the fifth or sixth day after their arrival the brothers did not appear for breakfast.
10142-8{_}1299{_}The Baroness immediately inquired in great anxiety if they had left the castle, but nobody seemed to have noticed them.
10142-8{_}1300{_}Apollonie was the only one who had seen them going upstairs together in the early morning, so she was sent up to look for them in the tower rooms.
10142-8{_}1301{_}When she found them empty, she opened the door of the old fencing-hall by some strange impulse.
10142-8{_}1302{_}Here Salo was crouching half fainting on the floor.
10142-8{_}1303{_}He told her that it was nothing to worry about, and that he had only lost consciousness for a moment.
10142-8{_}1304{_}She had to help him to get up, however, and he came downstairs supported on her arm.
10142-8{_}1305{_}The Baroness never said a word.
10142-8{_}1306{_}She stayed in her son's chamber till the physician who had been sent for had gone away again.
10142-8{_}1307{_}Then returning to us, she sat down beside Leonore and me and told us that we ought to know what had happened.
10142-8{_}1308{_}Apparently she was very calm, but I had never seen her face so pale.
10142-8{_}1309{_}She informed us that when she had spoken to her sons about their future plans, she had discovered that neither of them had ever spoken about it to the other.
10142-8{_}1310{_}Now they both declared to her that their full intention had been for years to come home after the completion of their studies and to live in Wildenstein with her and Leonore.
10142-8{_}1311{_}Bruno was quite beside himself when he found that Salo had apparently no intention to yield to him in the matter, so he challenged his brother to a duel in order to decide which of them was to remain at home.
10142-8{_}1312{_}Salo had been wounded and, losing consciousness, had fallen to the ground.
10142-8{_}1313{_}Bruno, fearing something worse, had disappeared.
10142-8{_}1314{_}The doctor had not found Sale's wounds of a serious nature, but as he had a delicate constitution, great care had to be taken.
10142-8{_}1315{_}When I left the castle that day I felt that all the joy and happiness I had ever known on earth was shattered, and this feeling stayed with me a long while after.
10142-8{_}1316{_}Soon after that sad event the Baroness got ready for a journey to the south, where she meant to go with Salo and Leonore.
10142-8{_}1317{_}Salo had not recovered as quickly as she had hoped, and Leonore, instead of getting more robust in our vigorous mountain-air, only became thinner and frailer.
10142-8{_}1318{_}Only once Bruno sent his mother some news.
10142-8{_}1319{_}In extremely few words he let her know that he was going to Spain, and that she need not trouble more about him.
10142-8{_}1320{_}But the news of his brother's survival reached him, nevertheless.
10142-8{_}1321{_}Now all those I had loved so passionately had gone away, and I felt it very deeply.
10142-8{_}1322{_}There the castle stood, sad and lifeless, and its lighted windows looked down no more upon us from the height.
10142-8{_}1323{_}All its eyes were closed and were to remain so."
10142-8{_}1324{_}"Oh, oh, did they never come back?"
10142-8{_}1325{_}cried out Kurt with regret.
10142-8{_}1326{_}"No, never," the mother replied.
10142-8{_}1327{_}"At that time, too, apparently, all the reports which had long ago faded were revived as to a ghost who was supposed to wander about the castle.
10142-8{_}1328{_}There were many who asserted they had seen or heard him, and till to-day the ghost of Wildenstein is haunting people's heads."
10142-8{_}1329{_}"Look at him," said Bruno dryly, pointing to the lower end of the table where Kurt was sitting.
10142-8{_}1330{_}"Finish, please, mother," the latter quickly urged.
10142-8{_}1331{_}"Where did they all get to?
10142-8{_}1332{_}And where is the brother who disappeared?"
10142-8{_}1333{_}"All I still have to tell you is short and sad," said the mother.
10142-8{_}1334{_}"Leonore faithfully wrote to me.
10142-8{_}1335{_}After spending the first winter in the south it became apparent that the Baroness's health was shattered.
10142-8{_}1336{_}She refused to return to the castle and sent her instructions to Apollonie, who had married the gardener of Wildenstein, and who now with her husband became caretaker of the castle, Three years afterwards the Baroness died without ever having returned.
10142-8{_}1337{_}A short time after that Leonore became Salo's wife, but they were not fated to remain together long.
10142-8{_}1338{_}Not more than three years later Salo died of a violent fever and Leonore followed him in a few months, but they left a little boy and a little girl.
10142-8{_}1339{_}After Salo's death Leonore was left alone in life, so an aunt from Holstein came to live with her in Nice.
10142-8{_}1340{_}After Leonore's death this aunt took the two children home with her.
10142-8{_}1341{_}I heard this from Apollonie, who had been sent Leonore's last instructions by this aunt.
10142-8{_}1342{_}I never learned anything further about the two children, and only once did I receive word from Baron Bruno through Apollonie.
10142-8{_}1343{_}Your late father, young Rector Bergmann, had married me just about the time when we heard of the Baroness's death.
10142-8{_}1344{_}I followed him very gladly to Sils, because Philip had just bought an estate there and was very anxious to have me close to him.
10142-8{_}1345{_}One day Apollonie came to me in great agitation.
10142-8{_}1346{_}Baron Bruno, never once sending word, had arrived in the castle after an absence of eight years and had brought with him a companion by the name of Mr. Demetrius.
10142-8{_}1347{_}The Baron had naturally expected to find his mother, his brother and his erstwhile playmates gathered there as before.
10142-8{_}1348{_}When he heard from Apollonie everything that had happened in his absence, he broke into a violent passion, because he believed that the news had been purposely kept from him.
10142-8{_}1349{_}Apollonie was able to show him his late mother's letters where she had given her exact orders in case of his return.
10142-8{_}1350{_}He could also see from them that she wrote to him frequently and had tried to reach him in vain.
10142-8{_}1351{_}Baron Bruno had lived an extremely unsettled existence and all the letters had miscarried, despite the orders he had left in big cities to have them forwarded.
10142-8{_}1352{_}Full of anger and bitterness the Baron immediately left, and till the present hour he has not been heard of.
10142-8{_}1353{_}Mr. Demetrius, later on called Mr. Trius by everybody, came back a few years ago to the deserted castle.
10142-8{_}1354{_}Apollonie had meanwhile lost her husband, had closed up all the rooms at the castle, and had gone to live again in the former gardener's cottage, where she is living now.
10142-8{_}1355{_}From the time when he reappeared till to-day, Mr. Trius has led a solitary life and sees no one except Apollonie, and her only when he is in need of her.
10142-8{_}1356{_}However hard Apollonie tried to make him tell about his master, he would not do it.
10142-8{_}1357{_}You know now about my happy life in Wildenstein and will be able to understand the reason why I moved here again after the death of your father.
10142-8{_}1358{_}Another inducement was that our dear Rector, an erstwhile friend of my father's, promised to give Bruno instruction which he could not get at a country school, so that I was able to keep him at home longer, you see.
10142-8{_}1359{_}Now you know why the deserted castle attracts me so despite its sad aspect, for it brings back to me my most beautiful memories."
10142-8{_}1360{_}"Oh, please, mother, tell us a little more," Kurt begged eagerly, when his mother rose.
10142-8{_}1361{_}"Oh, mother," Mea joined in, "tell us more about your friend, Leonore."
10142-8{_}1362{_}"Oh, yes, tell us more, mother," Bruno supplicated.
10142-8{_}1363{_}"There must be more to know still.
10142-8{_}1364{_}Did Baron Bruno keep on travelling in Spain?"
10142-8{_}1365{_}"I think most of the time, but I can't tell you for sure," the mother replied.
10142-8{_}1366{_}"I know everything only from Apollonie, who had these reports from Mr. Trius, but he either does not choose to talk or does not know very much himself about his master.
10142-8{_}1367{_}I have told you everything now and you must go to bed as quickly as you can.
10142-8{_}1368{_}It was your bedtime long ago."
10142-8{_}1369{_}No questions or supplications helped now, and soon the house was silent, except for the mother's quiet steps as she once more visited the children's beds.
10142-8{_}1370{_}Her eldest, who could become so violent, lay before her with a peaceful expression on his clear brow.
10142-8{_}1371{_}She knew how high his standard of honor was, but how would he end if his unfortunate trait gained more ascendancy over him?
10142-8{_}1372{_}Soon she would be obliged to send him away, and how could she hope for a loving influence in strange surroundings, which was the only thing to quiet him?
10142-8{_}1373{_}The mother knew that she had not the power to keep her children from pain and sin, but she knew the hand which leads and steadies all children that are entrusted to it, that can guard and save where no mother's hand or love can avail.
10142-8{_}1374{_}She went with folded hands from one bed to the other, surrendering her children to their Father's protection in Heaven.
10142-8{_}1375{_}He knew best how much they were in need of His loving care.
10142-8{_}1376{_}CHAPTER IV  AN UNEXPECTED APPARITION  Kurt had so many plans the next day that he already rushed to school as if he had not a minute to lose.
10142-8{_}1377{_}Mea and Lippo, who started with him, looked full of astonishment at his unusual speed.
10142-8{_}1378{_}Arriving at the school, he saw Loneli coming along with a drooping head and not, as usual, with a happy stride.
10142-8{_}1379{_}"What is it, Loneli?"
10142-8{_}1380{_}asked Kurt coming nearer.
10142-8{_}1381{_}"Why are your eyes swollen already before it is even eight o'clock?
10142-8{_}1382{_}Just he happy.
10142-8{_}1383{_}I'll help you.
10142-8{_}1384{_}Did anybody hurt you?"
10142-8{_}1385{_}"No, Kurt, no one, but I can't be happy any more," and with these words Loneli's eyes filled again with tears.
10142-8{_}1386{_}"I wish you could see grandmother since I've been on the shame-bench.
10142-8{_}1387{_}I would not mind if she were angry, for she generally forgives me again after a while; but she is sad all the time.
10142-8{_}1388{_}It is worst when I go to school in the morning, because she says that I brought down shame on us both, and that I have given her gray hairs.
10142-8{_}1389{_}She said to me that after having lived an honorable life and spent most of it with the most noble family, this was very hard for her.
10142-8{_}1390{_}She felt as if she had raised me only to bring down shame on both for the rest of our lives."
10142-8{_}1391{_}Loneli broke out anew into tears.
10142-8{_}1392{_}This neverending disgrace, together with the constant reproaches she had had to bear, seemed to choke her,  "No, no, Loneli, you don't need to cry any more.
10142-8{_}1393{_}It is not at all the way your grandmother is taking it," Kurt said consolingly.
10142-8{_}1394{_}"I'll go to her ever so soon to explain what happened.
10142-8{_}1395{_}Please be happy and everything will come out all right."
10142-8{_}1396{_}"Do you think so?"
10142-8{_}1397{_}Loneli asked, pleasantly surprised.
10142-8{_}1398{_}Her eyes were clear again, for she always believed whatever Kurt said to her.
10142-8{_}1399{_}Now he rushed over to the noisy crowd of children, who seemed to have been waiting for him.
10142-8{_}1400{_}Kurt was always glad to have such numerous friends, for he usually needed a large following for the execution of his schemes.
10142-8{_}1401{_}To-day he had two large undertakings in his head, and he needed to persuade his comrades to join him.
10142-8{_}1402{_}He was explaining with such violent gestures and eager words that they entirely neglected the first strokes of the tower bell.
10142-8{_}1403{_}At the last and eighth stroke the little crowd dispersed as suddenly as a flock of frightened birds.
10142-8{_}1404{_}Then they rushed into the school house.
10142-8{_}1405{_}Kurt was home to-day ahead of everybody, too.
10142-8{_}1406{_}He approached his mother with a large sheet of paper.
10142-8{_}1407{_}"Look, mother, Mr. Trius got a song.
10142-8{_}1408{_}Yesterday evening he threatened two more of my friends with the stick, but they were luckily able to save themselves.
10142-8{_}1409{_}It seems as if he had at least four eyes and ears which can see and hear whatever is going on.
10142-8{_}1410{_}I finished the song.
10142-8{_}1411{_}Can I read it to you?"
10142-8{_}1412{_}"I wish you had no friends that Mr. Trius has occasion to frighten with a stick," said the mother.
10142-8{_}1413{_}"I hope that it won't ever happen to you."
10142-8{_}1414{_}"Oh, he often threatens innocent people," Kurt replied.
10142-8{_}1415{_}"Listen to a true description of him."
10142-8{_}1416{_}A SONG ABOUT MR. TRIUS, THE BOY BEATER.
10142-8{_}1417{_}Old Trius lives in our town,    A haughty man is he,    And every one that he can catch    He beats right heartily.
10142-8{_}1418{_}Old Trius wears a yellow coat,    It's very long and thick,    But all the children run away    At sight of his big stick.
10142-8{_}1419{_}Old Trius of the pointed hat    He wanders all around,    And if he beats nobody, why    There's no one to be found.
10142-8{_}1420{_}Old Trius thinks: To spank a boy    Is really very kind,    And all he cannot hit in front    At least he hits behind.
10142-8{_}1421{_}Old Trius makes a pretty face    With every blow he gives.
10142-8{_}1422{_}He'll beat us all for many years,    I'm thinking, if he lives.
10142-8{_}1423{_}The mother could not help smiling a little bit during the perusal, but now she said seriously: "This song must under no condition fall into Mr. Trius' hands.
10142-8{_}1424{_}He might not look at it as a joke, and you must not offend him.
10142-8{_}1425{_}I advise you, Kurt, not to challenge Mr. Trius in any way, for he might reply to you in some unexpected fashion.
10142-8{_}1426{_}He has his own ways and means of getting rid of people."
10142-8{_}1427{_}Kurt was very anxious to get his mother's permission to run about that same evening by moonlight with his friends, and his mother granted it willingly.
10142-8{_}1428{_}"I hope you are not going on one of the unfortunate apple-expeditions I hear so much about," she added.
10142-8{_}1429{_}Kurt quite indignantly assured her that he would never do such a thing.
10142-8{_}1430{_}Lippo was pushing him to one side now.
10142-8{_}1431{_}The little boy had made attempts to reach his mother for several minutes, and he was delighted at his brother's quick departure.
10142-8{_}1432{_}"Mr. Rector sends you his regards and he wants to know if you wanted to give him an answer.
10142-8{_}1433{_}Here is a letter," said Lippo.
10142-8{_}1434{_}"Where did you bring the letter from?"
10142-8{_}1435{_}asked the mother.
10142-8{_}1436{_}"I didn't bring the letter.
10142-8{_}1437{_}Lise from the rectory brought it," was Lippo's information.
10142-8{_}1438{_}"But Lise saw me in front of the door and said that I should take the letter up with me and give it to you, and tell her whether you wanted to give the Rector an answer or not."
10142-8{_}1439{_}"Oh, that is just the way a message ought to be given," the mother said with a smile.
10142-8{_}1440{_}"Did you hear it, Mäzli?
10142-8{_}1441{_}I wish you could learn from Lippo how to do it.
10142-8{_}1442{_}Whenever you have one to give, I have such trouble to find out what really happened and what you have only imagined."
10142-8{_}1443{_}Mäzli, whose knitting-ball was at that moment in the most hopelessly knotted condition, was ever so glad when her mother suggested a new activity.
10142-8{_}1444{_}Quickly flinging her knitting away, she jumped up from her stool.
10142-8{_}1445{_}Then she began to repeat Lippo's speech, word for word: "I did not bring the letter.
10142-8{_}1446{_}Lise from the rectory--"  "No, no, Mäzli, I do not mean it that way," the mother interrupted her.
10142-8{_}1447{_}"I mean that the reports you bring me so often sound quite impossible.
10142-8{_}1448{_}I want you to be as careful and exact in them as Lippo."
10142-8{_}1449{_}In the meantime the mother had opened the letter and looked suddenly quite frightened.
10142-8{_}1450{_}"Tell the girl that I shall go to Mr. Rector myself and that she need not wait for an answer," was her message entrusted to Lippo.
10142-8{_}1451{_}The thing she had dreaded so much was settled now.
10142-8{_}1452{_}The Rector let her know in his letter that he had realized the time had come for his pupils to be put into different hands.
10142-8{_}1453{_}He wrote that he had decided to discontinue the studies with them next fall, but that he would be only too glad to be of assistance to Mrs. Maxa in consulting about Bruno's further education.
10142-8{_}1454{_}He closed with an assurance that he would be the happier to do so because Bruno had always been very dear to him.
10142-8{_}1455{_}Mrs. Maxa, sitting silently with folded hands, was lost in thought.
10142-8{_}1456{_}This was something that happened very seldom.
10142-8{_}1457{_}But Mea stood before her and trying to get her sympathy with passionate gestures.
10142-8{_}1458{_}"Just think, mother," she cried out, "Elvira is so angry now that she will never have anything more to do with me, no never.
10142-8{_}1459{_}But she was most offended because I told her that it was wrong of her; not to admit that she had chattered in school.
10142-8{_}1460{_}She said quite sarcastically that if I chose to correct her on account of that raggedy Loneli, I should keep Loneli for a friend and not her."
10142-8{_}1461{_}"Let her be for once," said the mother.
10142-8{_}1462{_}"Till now you have always gone after her; so do what she wishes this time.
10142-8{_}1463{_}It is wrong to call Loneli raggedy; few people are as honest and agreeable as Apollonie and her grandchild."
10142-8{_}1464{_}Mea was ready with many more complaints, for whenever anything bothered her, she felt the need to tell her mother.
10142-8{_}1465{_}She realized, though, that she had to put off further communications for a quiet evening hour.
10142-8{_}1466{_}Bruno had approached, and turning to his mother, asked in great suspense: "Mother, what did Mr. Rector write to you?
10142-8{_}1467{_}Have the plum-thieves been discovered?"
10142-8{_}1468{_}"I do not think that they have brought his decision about, but I am sure they hastened it.
10142-8{_}1469{_}Read the letter," said his mother, handing it to him.
10142-8{_}1470{_}"That is not so bad," Bruno said after reading it.
10142-8{_}1471{_}"As soon as you send me to town I shall be rid of them at last, and I won't have to bother about them any more.
10142-8{_}1472{_}You know, mother, that all they care about is to do mean and nasty things."
10142-8{_}1473{_}"But they will go to town, too, and then you will be thrown together.
10142-8{_}1474{_}There won't be anybody then who cares for you and will listen to you," the mother lamented.
10142-8{_}1475{_}"Do not worry, mother, the town is big and we won't be so close together.
10142-8{_}1476{_}I'll keep far enough away from them, you may be sure.
10142-8{_}1477{_}Don't let it trouble you," Bruno reassured her.
10142-8{_}1478{_}Kurt was so much occupied at lunch with his own plans and ideas that he never even noticed when his favorite dessert appeared on the table.
10142-8{_}1479{_}Lippo, seriously looking at him, said quite reproachfully, "Now you don't even see that we have apple-dumpling."
10142-8{_}1480{_}Such an indifference seemed wrong to the little boy.
10142-8{_}1481{_}But Kurt even swallowed the apple-dumpling absent-mindedly.
10142-8{_}1482{_}After lunch he begged his mother's permission to be allowed to leave immediately, because he still had so much to talk over with his friends.
10142-8{_}1483{_}"I'll tell you all about it afterwards, mother.
10142-8{_}1484{_}Be sure that I am doing something right that ought to be done," he reassured her.
10142-8{_}1485{_}"If only I can go now."
10142-8{_}1486{_}Having obtained permission, he shot away, and arriving at the school-house, flew into the midst of a crowd of boys.
10142-8{_}1487{_}But before their plan could be carried out the children were obliged to sit two whole hours on the school-benches.
10142-8{_}1488{_}It truly seemed to-day as if they would never end.
10142-8{_}1489{_}Lux, the sexton's boy, who preferred pulling the bell-rope and being violently drawn up by it to sitting in school, tapped his neighbor's sleeve.
10142-8{_}1490{_}"How late is it, Max?"
10142-8{_}1491{_}he asked.
10142-8{_}1492{_}"I don't know."
10142-8{_}1493{_}"Max," Lux whispered again, "the second expedition will be more fun than the first.
10142-8{_}1494{_}I look forward to it more, don't you?"
10142-8{_}1495{_}"You can look forward to the shame-bench if you don't keep quiet," Max retorted, squinting with his eyes in the direction of the teacher.
10142-8{_}1496{_}The latter had actually directed his eyes to the side where the whisperers sat.
10142-8{_}1497{_}Lux, bending over his book, kept quiet at last.
10142-8{_}1498{_}Finally the longed-for hour came and in a few minutes the whole swarm was outside.
10142-8{_}1499{_}With a great deal of noise, but in a quick and pretty orderly fashion they now formed a procession, which began to move in the direction of Apollonie's little house.
10142-8{_}1500{_}Here a halt was made.
10142-8{_}1501{_}Kurt, climbing to the top of a heap of logs, which lay in the pathway, stood upright, while the others grouped themselves about him.
10142-8{_}1502{_}Apollonie opened the window a little, but hid behind it, for she was wondering what was going on.
10142-8{_}1503{_}Loneli stood close behind her.
10142-8{_}1504{_}She had just come back breathlessly, for she had heard that a procession was coming towards her grandmother's house.
10142-8{_}1505{_}"Mrs. Apollonie," Kurt cried out with loud voice, "two whole classes from school have come to you to tell you that it was not Loneli's fault when she had to sit on the shame-bench.
10142-8{_}1506{_}It only happened because her character is so good.
10142-8{_}1507{_}Out of pure politeness she answered a question somebody asked her.
10142-8{_}1508{_}When the teacher wanted to know who was chattering, she honestly accused herself.
10142-8{_}1509{_}She did not tell him that she answered a question in fear of accusing somebody else.
10142-8{_}1510{_}We wanted to tell you all about it so that you won't think you have to be ashamed of Loneli.
10142-8{_}1511{_}We think and know that she is the friendliest and most obliging child in school."
10142-8{_}1512{_}"Long live Loneli!"
10142-8{_}1513{_}Lux suddenly cheered so that the whole band involuntarily joined him.
10142-8{_}1514{_}"Long live Loneli!
10142-8{_}1515{_};" it sounded again and the echo from the castle-mountain repeated, "Loneli."
10142-8{_}1516{_}Apollonie opened the window completely, and putting out her head, cried: "It is lovely of you, children that you don't want Loneli disgraced.
10142-8{_}1517{_}I thank you for justifying her.
10142-8{_}1518{_}Wait a minute.
10142-8{_}1519{_}I should like to do you a favor, too."
10142-8{_}1520{_}With that Apollonie disappeared from the window.
10142-8{_}1521{_}Soon after she came out by the door with a large basket of fragrant apples on her arm.
10142-8{_}1522{_}Putting it in front of the children, she said encouragingly, "Help yourselves."

10142-8{_}1526{_}"What on earth do you mean?"
10142-8{_}1527{_}Kurt cried out full of indignation.
10142-8{_}1528{_}"Mrs. Apollonie did not need to steal them.
10142-8{_}1529{_}Mr. Trius certainly could give her a few baskets of apples for all the shirts she sews and mends for him."
10142-8{_}1530{_}"Oh, I see, that is different," said Lux, now properly informed.
10142-8{_}1531{_}In the shortest time the huge basket was emptied of its delicious apples and the whole band had dispersed after many exclamations of thanks.
10142-8{_}1532{_}They all ran home and Kurt outran them all.
10142-8{_}1533{_}It was important now to do his home-work as speedily as possible, as the second expedition was to take place a little later.
10142-8{_}1534{_}When he reached the front door he noticed that Mrs. Knippel was coming up behind him.

10142-8{_}1536{_}After saying this he ran away.
10142-8{_}1537{_}Bruno and Mea, who were busy in the room with their work, did not find it necessary to follow Kurt's command.
10142-8{_}1538{_}If he found it so necessary, why didn't he do it himself, they thought, remaining seated.

10142-8{_}1542{_}Mäzli asked in a loud voice.

10142-8{_}1545{_}She always brought forward her most awful ideas when it was least suitable.
10142-8{_}1546{_}The mother, who was on the way already, entered just when Mea was running out with Mäzli.
10142-8{_}1547{_}Bruno also slipped quickly after them.
10142-8{_}1548{_}He had only waited for his mother's appearance in order to fly.
10142-8{_}1549{_}"Your children are certainly very peculiar," the district attorney's wife began.
10142-8{_}1550{_}"I have to think so every time I see them.
10142-8{_}1551{_}What do all your admonitions help, I should like to know?
10142-8{_}1552{_}Nature will have its way!
10142-8{_}1553{_}Not one of my children has ever been so impertinent, to say the least, as your little daughter is already."
10142-8{_}1554{_}"I am very sorry you should have to tell me that," Mrs. Maxa replied.

10142-8{_}1556{_}I hope you have never had a similar experience with my older children."

10142-8{_}1564{_}Mrs. Maxa confirmed the statement.

10142-8{_}1567{_}He will look for a suitable, attractive home in town that the three boys can move into next fall."

10142-8{_}1569{_}Mrs. Maxa said in consternation.

10142-8{_}1575{_}Mrs. Maxa was quite unable to hide her excitement.
10142-8{_}1576{_}"You can be reassured, for we have thought of that, too," the visitor said with a slightly superior smile.
10142-8{_}1577{_}"My husband's sister does not live very far from Mr. Falcon in Sils.

10142-8{_}1579{_}This calmed Mrs. Maxa a trifle, for her brother knew already how it stood between the three comrades and how little she wanted them to live together.
10142-8{_}1580{_}But she could not help wondering why these people were trying to force the boys to live together.
10142-8{_}1581{_}"I do not really understand why the boys should have to live together," she said with animation; "they do not profess to feel much friendship for each other, and never seek each other out.
10142-8{_}1582{_}You yourself, Mrs. Knippel, do not seem to get a very good impression from my children's ways.

10142-8{_}1586{_}Everybody would think that something special had happened between the families.
10142-8{_}1587{_}Both parties will only gain in respect by joining."
10142-8{_}1588{_}"I do not believe that people in the city will be interested in what the three boys are doing," said Mrs. Maxa, smiling a little.
10142-8{_}1589{_}That same moment the door was flung wide open.

10142-8{_}1591{_}The latter hastily retreated.
10142-8{_}1592{_}"No, no, Mäzli," she said quite frightened, "you should have told me that there was company."
10142-8{_}1593{_}Mrs. Knippel had risen to take her departure: "It seems to me that other visitors are greeted very joyfully by your children.
10142-8{_}1594{_}Well, I must say they have rather odd tastes," she said, walking towards the door.
10142-8{_}1595{_}"Apollonie is a very old friend of ours.
10142-8{_}1596{_}All the children love her very much.
10142-8{_}1597{_}They may have inherited this attachment, though," Mrs. Maxa replied with a smile.
10142-8{_}1598{_}"I only want to say one more word," said the lady turning round before stepping outside the door.
10142-8{_}1599{_}"The scene your son Kurt enacted to-day in front of Apollonie's cottage with his crowd of miscellaneous friends can only be called a vulgar noise."
10142-8{_}1600{_}But Mrs. Maxa did not yet know what Kurt had done.
10142-8{_}1601{_}The visitor turned to go now, as it seemed not worth her while to waste words about it.
10142-8{_}1602{_}As soon as the field was clear, Mäzli rushed out of a hiding-place, pulling Apollonie with her.
10142-8{_}1603{_}The old woman was terribly apologetic about having gone into the room.
10142-8{_}1604{_}When she had told Mäzli that she wanted to see her mother, the little girl had taken her there without any further ado.
10142-8{_}1605{_}She informed the Rector's widow that she had come to her with a quite incredible communication.
10142-8{_}1606{_}Mrs. Maxa found it necessary at this point to interrupt her friend.
10142-8{_}1607{_}She had noticed that Mäzli was all ears to what was coming.

10142-8{_}1610{_}Apollonie's communication took a considerable time.
10142-8{_}1611{_}She had just left when the family sat down to a belated supper.
10142-8{_}1612{_}Kurt swallowed his meal with signs of immoderate impatience.
10142-8{_}1613{_}As soon as possible he rushed away, after having given his promise not to come home late.
10142-8{_}1614{_}The friends that were to join him in this expedition had to be sought out first.
10142-8{_}1615{_}When he neared the meeting place, he felt a little disappointed.

10142-8{_}1617{_}This certainly was not the crowd he had had together at noon when at least all the boys had promised to take part in his new enterprise.
10142-8{_}1618{_}"They were afraid, they were afraid," all voices cried together.
10142-8{_}1619{_}Kurt heard now, while each screamed louder than the other that many boys and girls had left when the darkness was beginning to fall.
10142-8{_}1620{_}Among the few that were left there were only four girls.
10142-8{_}1621{_}"It doesn't matter," said Kurt.
10142-8{_}1622{_}"There are enough people still.
10142-8{_}1623{_}Whoever is afraid may leave.
10142-8{_}1624{_}We must start, though, because we have rather far to go.
10142-8{_}1625{_}We are not going up the well-known path, because Mr. Trius watches for apple-hunters there till midnight, I think.
10142-8{_}1626{_}That suits us exactly, for he must not hear us.
10142-8{_}1627{_}We are going up to the woods at the back of the castle.
10142-8{_}1628{_}First, we'll sing our challenge, then comes the pause, to give the ghost enough time, then again and after that for the third and last time.
10142-8{_}1629{_}If there really is a ghost, he will have appeared by then.

10142-8{_}1631{_}So when he hasn't come, we can tell everybody what we did.
10142-8{_}1632{_}Then they'll see that it is only a superstition and that there is no wandering ghost in Wildenstein.
10142-8{_}1633{_}Forward now!"
10142-8{_}1634{_}The little crowd set out full of spirits and eagerness for the adventure, for Kurt had clearly shown them that there could be no ghost.
10142-8{_}1635{_}To go up there and sing loudly to a non-existent ghost was capital fun.
10142-8{_}1636{_}Furthermore, they looked forward to boasting of their daring deed afterwards.
10142-8{_}1637{_}Faster and faster they climbed, so that only half of the usual time was taken in reaching their destination.
10142-8{_}1638{_}It was dark at first, but the moon suddenly came out from behind the clouds, cheerfully lighting up the fields.
10142-8{_}1639{_}Having reached the rear of the castle hill, they hurried up the incline and into the pinewoods, where the trees stood extremely close together.
10142-8{_}1640{_}This made it very dark, despite the fact that the wood was small.

10142-8{_}1642{_}Here and there one of the children sneaked off and did not reappear.
10142-8{_}1643{_}Three of the girls, after mysteriously whispering together, were gone, too, and with them several more stole away, for there was a strange rustling in the bushes.
10142-8{_}1644{_}Kurt with Lux and his enterprising sister Clevi were at the extreme front.
10142-8{_}1645{_}When it became very still, Kurt turned around.
10142-8{_}1646{_}"Come along!
10142-8{_}1647{_}Where are you all?"
10142-8{_}1648{_}he called back.
10142-8{_}1649{_}"We are coming," several voices answered from some children immediately behind him.
10142-8{_}1650{_}It was Max, Hans and Simi, and then Stoffi and Rudi behind them, but they were all.

10142-8{_}1652{_}"Where is the whole troup?"
10142-8{_}1653{_}asked Kurt.
10142-8{_}1654{_}"Let us wait till they catch up.
10142-8{_}1655{_}We must all stay together up there."
10142-8{_}1656{_}But none followed.
10142-8{_}1657{_}All the answer Kurt got to his question was the screaching of an owl.

10142-8{_}1659{_}"They were there, though, when we came into the woods."
10142-8{_}1660{_}"The cowards!"
10142-8{_}1661{_}Clevi cried indignantly,  "To be afraid of trees!
10142-8{_}1662{_}That certainly is funny."
10142-8{_}1663{_}"Well, we aren't afraid anyway; otherwise we shouldn't be here any more.
10142-8{_}1664{_}Call to those who are gone," Max called back.
10142-8{_}1665{_}"Come on now, come!"
10142-8{_}1666{_}Kurt commanded.
10142-8{_}1667{_}"There are eight of us left to sing, so we must all sing very loud."
10142-8{_}1668{_}On they went speedily till they could see the end of the woods.
10142-8{_}1669{_}One of the gray towers was peering between the trees.

10142-8{_}1672{_}said Kurt, "but we must not go outside the woods.
10142-8{_}1673{_}The Wildenstein ghost might otherwise step up to us, if he walks around the terrace.
10142-8{_}1674{_}Here we go!"
10142-8{_}1675{_}Kurt began and all the others vigorously joined him:     Come out, you ghost of Wildenstein!
10142-8{_}1676{_}For we are not afraid,    We've come here in the bright moonshine      To sing the song we've made    Come out, come out, and leave your den;      You'll never scare the folks again.
10142-8{_}1677{_}Everything was quiet roundabout, only the night wind was soughing in the old pine-trees.
10142-8{_}1678{_}Between them there was a clear view of the terrace, which the moon was now flooding with light; the space before the castle lay peaceful and deserted.
10142-8{_}1679{_}"We must sing again," said Kurt.
10142-8{_}1680{_}"He didn't hear us.
10142-8{_}1681{_}If he doesn't give us an answer this time we'll tell him what we know.
10142-8{_}1682{_}Then we'll sing fearfully loud:     Hurrah!
