10142-8{_}2511{_}You can retire if you prefer.
10142-8{_}2512{_}You go upstairs to the room at the right corner."
10142-8{_}2513{_}"Oh, no, I want to stay as long as anybody is left," Salo replied.
10142-8{_}2514{_}"I shall enjoy singing and doing everything with you.
10142-8{_}2515{_}It is all so funny and strange."
10142-8{_}2516{_}Kurt had chosen a suitable song and Uncle Philip began it so vigorously that everybody could join and a full-voiced chorus was formed.
10142-8{_}2517{_}Lippo's voice sounded dreadfully weak, but he sang every note to the last word, fighting mightily against his growing sleepiness.
10142-8{_}2518{_}Now the little company could wander upstairs to their respective rooms without further obstacle.
10142-8{_}2519{_}"Oh," Uncle Philip breathed relieved when they had reached the top.
10142-8{_}2520{_}"At least we are as far as this.
10142-8{_}2521{_}It really is an undertaking to keep in order a handful of children where one always differs from the last.
10142-8{_}2522{_}Now I have luckily gotten through for today.
10142-8{_}2523{_}What?
10142-8{_}2524{_}Not yet?
10142-8{_}2525{_}What is the matter, Bruno?"
10142-8{_}2526{_}The latter, approaching his uncle with clear signs that he wanted him for something, had pulled him aside.
10142-8{_}2527{_}"I want to ask you for something," said Bruno.
10142-8{_}2528{_}"I wonder if you will do me a great favor, Uncle Philip.
10142-8{_}2529{_}Salo and I have so much to talk about still and he must leave to-morrow, I wanted to ask you if Kurt can sleep beside you in the guest room and Salo could sleep in Kurt's bed in my room."
10142-8{_}2530{_}"What are you thinking of," the uncle said irritably.
10142-8{_}2531{_}"You should hear what your mother would say to that.
10142-8{_}2532{_}The idea of having a Wallerstätten for a guest and offering him a bed which has been used already.
10142-8{_}2533{_}That would seem a real crime in her eyes.
10142-8{_}2534{_}That can't be; no, it mustn't.
10142-8{_}2535{_}I hope you can see it, too, don't you?"
10142-8{_}2536{_}"Yes," Bruno said, much depressed, for he had to agree.
10142-8{_}2537{_}But Uncle could not stand such downcast spirits.
10142-8{_}2538{_}"Listen, Bruno," he said, "you realize that we can't do it that way.
10142-8{_}2539{_}But an uncle knows how to arrange things and that is why he is here.
10142-8{_}2540{_}This is the way we'll do.
10142-8{_}2541{_}I'll sleep in your bed, and Salo and you can sleep in the guest-room.
10142-8{_}2542{_}Will that suit?"
10142-8{_}2543{_}"Oh, thank you, Uncle Philip!
10142-8{_}2544{_}There is no other uncle like you," Bruno cried out in his enthusiasm.
10142-8{_}2545{_}So Uncle Philip's last difficulty was solved for to-day and everybody was willing to go to bed.
10142-8{_}2546{_}Soon the house lay in deep quiet: even the sick child in the highest story lay calmly sleeping on her cool pillows.
10142-8{_}2547{_}She did not even notice when Mrs. Maxa stepped up once more to her bedside with a little lamp.
10142-8{_}2548{_}Before herself retiring she wanted to listen once more to the child's breathing.
10142-8{_}2549{_}Only the two new friends were still talking long after midnight.
10142-8{_}2550{_}They understood each other so thoroughly and upon all points that Bruno had proposed in his enthusiasm that they would not waste one minute of the night in sleep.
10142-8{_}2551{_}Salo expressed his wish over and over again that Bruno might become his comrade in the boarding school.
10142-8{_}2552{_}But finally victorious sleep stole unperceived over the two lads and quietly closed their eyes.
10142-8{_}2553{_}CHAPTER VII  THE MOTHER'S ABSENCE HAS CONSEQUENCES  Next morning Salo was allowed to go into his sister's room in order to say good-bye to her.
10142-8{_}2554{_}She looked at him so cheerfully that he asked with eager delight, "Do you feel so much better already, Leonore?"
10142-8{_}2555{_}"Oh, yes, I feel as if I were at home," she replied with shining eyes.
10142-8{_}2556{_}"I feel as if our mother had come down from heaven to take care of me."
10142-8{_}2557{_}"When you can get up and go downstairs you will be happier still.
10142-8{_}2558{_}I know how much you will enjoy meeting the whole family," said Salo.
10142-8{_}2559{_}"Then you will feel as if you were in a real home that belongs to you."
10142-8{_}2560{_}"It is such a shame that you have to go," Leonore sighed, but this time the tears did not come quite so urgently.
10142-8{_}2561{_}How things had changed since yesterday--how different it was now to stay behind!
10142-8{_}2562{_}At this moment Mrs. Maxa entered the room.
10142-8{_}2563{_}She had left it as she wanted to give brother and sister an opportunity to see each other alone, but the time had come for Salo to depart, and he was obliged to leave his sister.
10142-8{_}2564{_}To-day it seemed harder for him to go away than leave Leonore behind.
10142-8{_}2565{_}"I can't even say that I wish you to come soon.
10142-8{_}2566{_}I have to hope that you can remain here a long while," he said cheerily, while Leonore was smiling bravely.
10142-8{_}2567{_}Uncle Philip, ready for the journey, stood beside the carriage.
10142-8{_}2568{_}All the children ran towards Salo as soon as he appeared, and when he said good-bye, he was treated like a friend of the family of many years' standing.
10142-8{_}2569{_}Each of the children showed his grief in a special manner.
10142-8{_}2570{_}Mäzli cried loudly over and over again, "Oh, Salo, please come soon again, please come soon again."
10142-8{_}2571{_}When the carriage was rolling away and the handkerchiefs that fluttered him last greetings were all Salo could see from the distance, he rapidly brushed away a few tears.
10142-8{_}2572{_}He had never felt so thoroughly at home anywhere in the world before.
10142-8{_}2573{_}How happy he had been!
10142-8{_}2574{_}The thought of going far away and possibly never coming back gave him a little pang of grief.
10142-8{_}2575{_}When the children returned at noon from school they were still full of their vivid impression of Salo's sudden appearance and departure.
10142-8{_}2576{_}They were all anxious to tell their mother about it, because they knew that they could always count on her lively sympathy.
10142-8{_}2577{_}One or the other of the children kept forgetting that the mother must not be sought and would absent-mindedly make an attempt to go upstairs, but they were always met by unexpected resistance.
10142-8{_}2578{_}Lippo on his arrival home from school had posted himself there to see that his mother's orders were strictly kept.
10142-8{_}2579{_}He also had missed her desperately, but he had nevertheless remembered her injunctions and was quite certain that the others might forget and act contrary to her orders.
10142-8{_}2580{_}Placing himself on the first step, he would hold any of his brothers or sisters with both hands when they came towards him as they dashed upstairs.
10142-8{_}2581{_}When he cried out loudly, "We mustn't do it, we mustn't do it," they ran away again, quite frightened, for his horrified shrieks might have penetrated into the sick-room.
10142-8{_}2582{_}Kathy was the only one who appreciated Lippo's worth.
10142-8{_}2583{_}She had received orders to remind the children of the strict command, and she knew quite well from previous experiences that she could never have succeeded as effectively as he.
10142-8{_}2584{_}Mäzli, meanwhile, was sitting at Apollonie's table, gayly eating a snow-white milk-pudding which Apollonie knew so well how to prepare.
10142-8{_}2585{_}Whenever Mäzli came to a meal at her house, she always set this favorite dish before the child.
10142-8{_}2586{_}The days when Mäzli came for a visit here were happy days for Loneli.
10142-8{_}2587{_}There was always something funny going on at meal-time, because Mäzli had so many amusing things to speak about.
10142-8{_}2588{_}On those days she was never obliged to tell her grandmother exactly what lessons she had known in school and which she had not.
10142-8{_}2589{_}Usually Apollonie was dreadfully anxious to hear how punctually she had fulfilled her duties, and she always chose lunch-time for that purpose because then no other affair interfered with talking.
10142-8{_}2590{_}Beaming with joy, Loneli now sat beside Mäzli, who was telling uninterruptedly about Salo.
10142-8{_}2591{_}She told them that he was friendlier and nicer than any boy she had ever seen, and she quoted Bruno, Mea and Kurt as saying exactly the same thing.
10142-8{_}2592{_}Usually they disagreed on such points.
10142-8{_}2593{_}Apollonie was quite absorbed in listening, too, and nodding her head once in a while, she seemed to say: "Yes, yes, I know that he couldn't be called Salo for nothing."
10142-8{_}2594{_}This interesting subject of conversation kept her longer than usual to-day.
10142-8{_}2595{_}"Suddenly she started up, quite frightened.
10142-8{_}2596{_}Oh, is it possible?
10142-8{_}2597{_}It is nearly one o'clock.
10142-8{_}2598{_}Hurry up, Loneli, or you'll be late for school.
10142-8{_}2599{_}Mäzli, you and I have something to do, too, this afternoon.
10142-8{_}2600{_}I shall take you on a walk and I'll tell you where we are going as soon as we start."
10142-8{_}2601{_}As the dishes had to be washed first, Apollonie thought that Mäzli might go out to play in the garden.
10142-8{_}2602{_}But Mäzli preferred to see the plates washed and dried and afterwards set in neat rows.
10142-8{_}2603{_}After these tasks Apollonie put on a good apron, a beautiful neck-cloth, and after packing up several shirts, cloths and stockings into a large basket the two set out.
10142-8{_}2604{_}"Where are we going?"
10142-8{_}2605{_}Mäzli asked, inspecting the basket.

10142-8{_}2607{_}"They belong to Mr. Trius," replied Apollonie.
10142-8{_}2608{_}"We are going all the way up to the castle, as far as the great iron door.

10142-8{_}2610{_}You'll be able to peep in through the door till he comes back again with the empty basket."

10142-8{_}2612{_}Mäzli asked.

10142-8{_}2614{_}It would take a long time nowadays to find even a couple of the flowers."
10142-8{_}2615{_}"We could surely find them inside," Mäzli said with great certainty.
10142-8{_}2616{_}"But Mäzli, what are you thinking of?
10142-8{_}2617{_}Nobody is allowed to go in.

10142-8{_}2632{_}He is the master there and can give orders, and people must not disobey him.
10142-8{_}2633{_}Look, one can see the open windows quite plainly now."

10142-8{_}2635{_}asked Mäzli peeping up searchingly.

10142-8{_}2645{_}Everything is growing wild.

10142-8{_}2675{_}"What, nothing?

10142-8{_}2710{_}Mr. Trius had suddenly grown more lively.

10142-8{_}2719{_}But he had quickly been lost from view.
10142-8{_}2720{_}While Apollonie and Mr. Trius had been absorbed in their violent altercation and had stared at each other, she in wild excitement and he in stiff immovability, Mäzli had slipped from between the two as swiftly as a little mouse.

10142-8{_}2723{_}This was not what Mäzli had expected, so she went up to the terrace of the castle and looked about from there for the flower garden.

10142-8{_}2938{_}This term suited him exactly, as he had a secret hope of prolonging it somewhat.

10142-8{_}2940{_}The mother had been quite certain that Bruno in his interview with her would make a last, desperate effort to escape having to live with the Knippel boys.

10142-8{_}2942{_}Bruno's thoughts were constantly occupied by the thought that his new, charming friend stood entirely alone in the world.

10142-8{_}2946{_}She had no authority over the children and could therefore do nothing, as everything depended on Salo's early completion of his studies so that he could choose an occupation.
10142-8{_}2947{_}This would have to be settled by the gentleman of whom Salo had spoken.
10142-8{_}2948{_}He was probably a relation of their mother's who had undertaken the care of the children.
10142-8{_}2949{_}Bruno was terribly cast down when he heard this.
10142-8{_}2950{_}When his mother did not give him help and counsel right away, she usually gave him some hope by saying, "We shall see."

10142-8{_}2958{_}All the girls in the boarding school had always accused her of that, for she was often terribly unhappy, and she could not help it.

10142-8{_}2964{_}Mea had to laugh over this speech, which little resembled her mother's style of talking.

10142-8{_}2968{_}Leonore has such a delicate, refined nature that it might frighten her to see you carried away by such passion, Mea."
10142-8{_}2969{_}When the doctor came back again in two days he was surprised at the improved condition of his little patient.
10142-8{_}2970{_}"If she was not so very young," the doctor said to Mrs. Maxa while she accompanied him out of the room, "I should say that her illness came largely from some hidden sorrow and inner suffering.
10142-8{_}2971{_}She has apparently been able to shake it off in the good care and affectionate treatment she is getting here.
10142-8{_}2972{_}But I can scarcely believe this of a child."
10142-8{_}2973{_}When Mrs. Maxa asked him how soon Leonore could leave the room and spend the day with her very active children, he answered, "She can do it from to-morrow on.
10142-8{_}2974{_}Nothing can possibly refresh her more than some lively playmates."
10142-8{_}2975{_}With this he took his leave.
10142-8{_}2976{_}Going downstairs, he met Apollonie, who was just coming up with a supper-tray laden with delicate dishes for the sick child.
10142-8{_}2977{_}"That is right," said the doctor; "it gives one an appetite only to look at it."
10142-8{_}2978{_}"Yes, the poor child eats like a little bird," said Apollonie; "but Mrs. Rector says that there must be things to choose from in order to tempt her.
10142-8{_}2979{_}How is she getting along, doctor?
10142-8{_}2980{_}Do you think she'll get well again?
10142-8{_}2981{_}Isn't she just like a little angel?"
10142-8{_}2982{_}"That is hard for me to say, as I do not know any angels," he said smiling, "but she might be for all I know.
10142-8{_}2983{_}I am sure that she will get well with careful nursing, and you are sure to see to that, Mrs. Apollonie.
10142-8{_}2984{_}You seem to think that in being given care of the child you have drawn the big prize in the lottery."
10142-8{_}2985{_}"Indeed I have.
10142-8{_}2986{_}I really have," she cried after him.
10142-8{_}2987{_}No event had ever been looked forward to with such great suspense in Mrs. Maxa's house as the appearance of Leonore.
10142-8{_}2988{_}As soon as all the children were home from school the next morning, their mother fetched her down.
10142-8{_}2989{_}The three older ones were standing expectantly together in a little group, while the two smaller ones had placed themselves with wide-open eyes near the door.
10142-8{_}2990{_}Leonore, entering, greeted one after the other in such an engaging, confidential way that she made them feel as if they were old friends.
10142-8{_}2991{_}She loved their mother so much and had been so closely drawn to her that she was fond of the children before she had even seen them.
10142-8{_}2992{_}This pleased them tremendously, for they had expected Leonore to be very different from themselves and had been rather afraid of her.
10142-8{_}2993{_}As soon as they saw her, they felt that they might each be special friends with their charming guest.
10142-8{_}2994{_}Leonore found herself surrounded by them all in a corner of the sofa.
10142-8{_}2995{_}As she did not look at all strong yet, the mother had led her there.
10142-8{_}2996{_}Leonore tried to answer all the questions, listen to all the projects and information which were showered upon her, while her eyes danced with merriment.
10142-8{_}2997{_}These unusual surroundings made Leonore so happy that her face became quite rosy.
10142-8{_}2998{_}Mea had been already completed in her mind a plan which, if it succeeded, would make it possible for her to have Leonore to herself sometimes.
10142-8{_}2999{_}Since all her brothers and sisters liked the visitor so much, it was not easy to get her off alone.
10142-8{_}3000{_}If only her mother would sanction the plan!
10142-8{_}3001{_}That day Mea had to set the table, and when lunch time had come, she quickly ran to her mother to ask her if she might take Apollonie's place in Leonore's room, and to her great delight she willingly consented.
10142-8{_}3002{_}Mea told her she would only be too glad to wait on Leonore at night if she could but be with her.
10142-8{_}3003{_}Leonore really needed no more special care, and in case of an emergency Mea could easily run down to fetch her mother.
10142-8{_}3004{_}"Leonore will mean more to you than she will ever realize," the mother concluded, "and I feel very gratified if you can do something for her, too."
10142-8{_}3005{_}Mrs. Maxa then informed Apollonie of the new plan, and she felt sure that the latter would be glad to get home again.
10142-8{_}3006{_}"I do everything in my power for that angel," she exclaimed.
10142-8{_}3007{_}"I should go to live in the desert if only I could procure a home for her."
10142-8{_}3008{_}After dinner she went to Leonore to say good-bye, and the child pressed her hand most warmly, thanking her for the good care she had received.
10142-8{_}3009{_}"I shall never forget how kind you have been, Apollonie," she said heartily.
10142-8{_}3010{_}"I shall come to see you as soon as I am allowed to go.
10142-8{_}3011{_}I hope that we shall see each other very often."
10142-8{_}3012{_}"Oh, yes, I hope so!
10142-8{_}3013{_}Please ask Mrs. Rector to let you come to me as often as possible," said Apollonie before leaving.
10142-8{_}3014{_}Leonore now told the children that Apollonie had very vividly described to her the lovely home of her parents and the wonderful life in the castle.
10142-8{_}3015{_}She had said frankly that she would never desire such a fine home, if only Salo and she could call a little house their own, so the good-hearted Apollonie had suggested that they might live with her.
10142-8{_}3016{_}She could easily let them have the whole cottage with the exception of a tiny chamber.
10142-8{_}3017{_}She could wait on them, and what more could they desire?
10142-8{_}3018{_}Leonore had felt that this would be better than anything she had dreamed of, as she could come over to Mrs. Maxa and her children as often as she pleased.
10142-8{_}3019{_}How happy Salo would be if she wrote him about it.
10142-8{_}3020{_}"Yes, you can," Mäzli declared.
10142-8{_}3021{_}"Her house is a lovely place to live in.
10142-8{_}3022{_}Loneli is there, who does everything one wants her to, and Apollonie always cooks what one likes best."
10142-8{_}3023{_}Kurt made a little enigmatical remark to Mäzli about her greed, but before she could have it explained to her, the mother turned to Leonore.
10142-8{_}3024{_}"I do not want you to be deluded by this thought, dear child," she said, "for that might only bring you disappointment.
10142-8{_}3025{_}As soon as you are well, you can walk to Apollonie's cottage and then you will see what a tiny place it is.
10142-8{_}3026{_}The great obstacle of Salo's studies would not be put aside in that way, either, for he could not join you there for years."
10142-8{_}3027{_}"Oh, I was thinking all the time how lovely it would be to live with Apollonie!
10142-8{_}3028{_}It would be so wonderful--I could live with her there and Salo could come to us in the holidays till he is through with his studies.
10142-8{_}3029{_}Then we could both settle here in the neighborhood."
10142-8{_}3030{_}Leonore had been counting on this new scheme and she looked up at Mrs. Maxa as if she longed for her consent.
10142-8{_}3031{_}As Mrs. Maxa did not have the heart to shatter the child's hopes completely, she decided to let the matter rest for the present.
10142-8{_}3032{_}As soon as they could visit Apollonie, Leonore could judge for herself how impossible the plan was.
10142-8{_}3033{_}Leonore's eyes were usually very sad, but occasionally she would look quite merry, and it was so that she appeared that evening when the children were surrounding her on all sides.
10142-8{_}3034{_}When each had to tell her so much and tried to be nearest her, she experienced the feeling that she had come to a family to which she really belonged.
10142-8{_}3035{_}Each of the children had founded a special relation with Leonore.
10142-8{_}3036{_}Bruno saw himself as her protector and adviser, and as her brother's close friend he meant to keep an active watch over her.
10142-8{_}3037{_}Mea, whose thoughts had been completely absorbed for days in her new friend, brought her all the warmth of a heart which craved friendship passionately.
10142-8{_}3038{_}Kurt had made it his duty to cheer up the rather melancholy child as much as was in his power.
10142-8{_}3039{_}Lippo, still filled a little with his post of sentinel, always came close to her as if he still needed to watch over her.
10142-8{_}3040{_}Mäzli was of the firm opinion that she had to entertain the guest, so she would relate fragments of funny things she knew, passing from one to another.
10142-8{_}3041{_}In this way Leonore got to hear of the Knippel family.
10142-8{_}3042{_}The time passed so quickly that loud laments were heard when the mother announced that it was time for Leonore to retire.
10142-8{_}3043{_}She did not want her strength to be overtaxed on her first day out of bed.
10142-8{_}3044{_}"We shall have many more days after this when we can be together," she added.
10142-8{_}3045{_}"Let us be glad of that."
10142-8{_}3046{_}"There might not be so many, for I feel quite well already," Leonore said with a sigh.
10142-8{_}3047{_}Mrs. Maxa smiled.
10142-8{_}3048{_}"We must thank God for that.
10142-8{_}3049{_}But you need to get strong, and I hope that you may find the needed recreation and change here."
10142-8{_}3050{_}Then she accompanied the two girls up to their room at the top of the house.
10142-8{_}3051{_}As Mea was to be Leonore's sole nurse from now on, Mrs. Maxa wanted to reassure herself that nothing was missing.
10142-8{_}3052{_}It was in Mea's nature to endow every new friend with marvellous qualities.
10142-8{_}3053{_}Her imagination was always as active as her heart, which she gave unreservedly on such occasions.
10142-8{_}3054{_}Unfortunately Mea suffered many disappointments in that way, because on nearer acquaintance her friends very seldom came up to her expectations.
10142-8{_}3055{_}She always tried hard to hold on to the original image, even if it did not in the least coincide with what her friends proved to be in reality and this brought on numberless fights with Kurt, who, with his usual shrewdness, could not help revealing to her the real state of affairs.
10142-8{_}3056{_}This always disillusioned her finally, for it was hard to deny his proofs.
10142-8{_}3057{_}Whenever another girl woke a passionate love in her, she was bound to expect something unusual from her.
10142-8{_}3058{_}A week had passed since Leonore had spent her first day as convalescent among the family.
10142-8{_}3059{_}As Mea had the privilege of being in the closest, most intimate contact with her new friend in the late evening hours, she was in a state of perfect bliss.
10142-8{_}3060{_}Every moment of the day that she was home she tried to be at Leonore's side and in her walks to and from school there existed for her no other subject of conversation than Leonore.
10142-8{_}3061{_}It was quite unusual that Kurt had not produced a rhyme about her great devotion.
10142-8{_}3062{_}He had not once said: "Things will be different after a while."
10142-8{_}3063{_}Brother and sister this time were entirely of one opinion about her: it even seemed as if Kurt himself had caught a touch of the friendship fever, as he used to call Mea's great devotion.
10142-8{_}3064{_}Apparently Bruno was of the same opinion, too.
10142-8{_}3065{_}In all his free hours he used to sit in a corner of the room with his books, paying no attention to anything else, but since Leonore had come he always joined the merry group and generally had something to relate or to show for Leonore's entertainment.
10142-8{_}3066{_}This he did in a quiet, gentler manner, such that it seemed as if he would hardly have behaved otherwise.
10142-8{_}3067{_}Lippo felt so comfortable in Leonore's presence that he always kept as close to her as possible.
10142-8{_}3068{_}Even when he told his experiences at great length, she never became impatient, but encouraged him to go on when his brothers and sisters made sarcastic remarks about him.
10142-8{_}3069{_}From time to time he would confidentially say to her: "Just stay with us always, Leonore.
10142-8{_}3070{_}You are at home here now, even if you have no home anywhere else."
10142-8{_}3071{_}This was uttered in a spirit of utter conviction, as the little boy had heard it from her own lips and was sure that this would be the best for them all.
10142-8{_}3072{_}Leonore blushed a deep scarlet at these words, as if Lippo had pronounced a thought she did not dare to foster in her own heart.
10142-8{_}3073{_}Once his mother had noticed this, so she told Lippo one evening, not to say this again.
10142-8{_}3074{_}As it was impossible to keep Leonore, it was much better not to speak of it, as it only gave her pain.
10142-8{_}3075{_}As this was a firm command, Lippo obeyed faithfully.
10142-8{_}3076{_}He kept on, however, showing Leonore that he loved to be with her.
10142-8{_}3077{_}Mäzli's love for Leonore showed itself more than anything in a wish to lend her a helping; hand in many things which the little girl felt her lovely friend stood in need of.
10142-8{_}3078{_}She had seen quite plainly that Leonore often became very sad when everyone else about her was laughing and she herself had been quite bright a moment before.
10142-8{_}3079{_}But Mäzli knew how she was going to help.
10142-8{_}3080{_}She meant to tell Apollonie how to fit up her cottage for Leonore and Salo, who, she hoped, would spend his holidays there, too.
10142-8{_}3081{_}She meant to superintend these preparations herself and to have it all fixed as daintily as possible.
10142-8{_}3082{_}By this time Mea's new friend was adored by the whole family, and they showed it by doing all in their power for her.
10142-8{_}3083{_}They had agreed that she differed absolutely from Mea's former friends.
10142-8{_}3084{_}They could not analyze wherein lay the charm which pervaded her whole personality.
10142-8{_}3085{_}The children had never known anybody who was so polite towards everyone, including Kathy, who only spoke affectionate, tender words, and always seemed so grateful when others were kind to her.
10142-8{_}3086{_}This spirit was something new and extremely delightful.
10142-8{_}3087{_}They had to admit to themselves that they wished everybody would act in such a way, as this would do away forever with the fights and altercations that had always arisen between them, and for which they were afterwards always sorry.
10142-8{_}3088{_}The only thing they would have been glad to change in Leonore were her sudden fits of gloom, which affected them all.
10142-8{_}3089{_}Leonore tried very hard to fight these depressing thoughts, but they went so deep that she seldom succeeded.
10142-8{_}3090{_}Their mother consoled them by saying that Leonore would get stronger as soon as she could take walks with them in the woods and meadows, and that feelings which now weighed on her would then seem lighter.
10142-8{_}3091{_}A few days later the children, including Leonore, came back with rosy cheeks and glowing eyes from their first walk to the surrounding hills.
10142-8{_}3092{_}The fresh mountain breeze had exhilarated them so much that the feeling of well-being was laughing from their young faces.
10142-8{_}3093{_}Even Leonore's cheeks, that were usually so pale, were faintly tinged with a rosy hue.
10142-8{_}3094{_}The mother stepped out of the garden into the road in order to welcome the children.
10142-8{_}3095{_}"Oh," she cried out joyfully.
10142-8{_}3096{_}"This first walk has been splendid.
10142-8{_}3097{_}Leonore looks like a fresh apple-blossom."
10142-8{_}3098{_}Taking her hand with great tenderness between her own, she gazed at her very closely in order to rejoice over the rosy color on the child's delicate face.
10142-8{_}3099{_}That moment a beggar-woman approached, holding by each hand a little girl.
10142-8{_}3100{_}The children's clothes were so ragged that their little bodies were scarcely covered.
10142-8{_}3101{_}Looking at Mrs. Maxa, the beggar-woman said, "Yes, yes, children can make one happy enough when one has a home.
10142-8{_}3102{_}You are a fortunate lady to have a good roof for your own.
10142-8{_}3103{_}It would be better for two such homeless ones as these not to exist!
10142-8{_}3104{_}They are sure to remain homeless all their lives, and that is the saddest thing of all."
10142-8{_}3105{_}With that she stretched out her hand, for Mrs. Maxa was looking at her intently.
10142-8{_}3106{_}Leonore had quickly taken off her shawl and jacket.
10142-8{_}3107{_}"May I give it to them?"
10142-8{_}3108{_}she asked Mrs. Maxa in a low voice.
10142-8{_}3109{_}The beggar-woman had already noticed the girl's gesture and stretched out her hands in her direction.
10142-8{_}3110{_}"I am glad, young lady, that you have pity for these homeless ones, even if you do not know what that means.
10142-8{_}3111{_}God bless you!"
10142-8{_}3112{_}Leonore looked imploringly into Mrs. Maxa's face.
10142-8{_}3113{_}The latter nodded, as it was too late now to explain to Leonore what action would have been better.
10142-8{_}3114{_}She made up her mind to do it afterwards for similar occasions.
10142-8{_}3115{_}With many words the poor woman thanked her for the gift.
10142-8{_}3116{_}She was very anxious to kiss the young lady's hand for the two garments, but Leonore had immediately run away.
10142-8{_}3117{_}Mea followed and found Leonore, who had been so merry on the walk, sitting in her sofa-corner, crying bitterly with her head between her hands.
10142-8{_}3118{_}"What is the matter, Leonore?
10142-8{_}3119{_}Why do you cry so terribly?"
10142-8{_}3120{_}Mea, asked, quite frightened.
10142-8{_}3121{_}She could not answer at once.
10142-8{_}3122{_}The mother and the other children had come in, too, and now they all surrounded the sobbing girl in great amazement and sympathy.

10142-8{_}3125{_}That is what the woman said, and I believe her.
10142-8{_}3126{_}How should one find a home if one can't look for one?"
10142-8{_}3127{_}Leonore had never before broken out into such passionate grief.
10142-8{_}3128{_}Mrs. Maxa looked at her very sorrowfully.
10142-8{_}3129{_}"She is a real Wallerstätten at the bottom of her heart," she said to herself.
10142-8{_}3130{_}"That will mean more struggles for her than I thought."
10142-8{_}3131{_}At a sign from her the children plainly understood that she asked them to go into the garden for a little while.

10142-8{_}3134{_}You told me that you found a song among your mother's music which always comforted you when you seemed to lose courage and confidence in God.
10142-8{_}3135{_}You said that it always made you feel that He was not forgetting you and your brother, and that he is looking after you in whatever way is best for you, even if you can't recognize it now.
10142-8{_}3136{_}Have you forgotten this?
10142-8{_}3137{_}Can you tell me your favorite verse in it?"

10142-8{_}3140{_}"It makes me happy because I know that God can do for us what Salo and I can't do for ourselves.
10142-8{_}3141{_}But when everything stays the same for so long and there is no prospect of any change, it is so hard to keep this faith.
10142-8{_}3142{_}If we can't do anything for ourselves, it seems as if everything would have to be that way.
10142-8{_}3143{_}The woman said that if anybody is homeless once, he has to remain that way for the rest of his life."
10142-8{_}3144{_}"No, no, Leonore," Mrs. Maxa answered, "you must not take a chance word seriously.

10142-8{_}3146{_}It is not true at all.
10142-8{_}3147{_}Of course you can't look ahead into your future, but you can ask God to give you full confidence in Him.
10142-8{_}3148{_}Then you can leave it all to Him, and the sense of His protection will make you calmer.
10142-8{_}3149{_}It will also keep you from making uncertain plans, which might only bring fresh disappointments."
10142-8{_}3150{_}Leonore had attentively followed every word Mrs. Maxa had uttered.
10142-8{_}3151{_}Looking thoughtfully in front of her for a moment, she said, "Aunt Maxa"--this was the mode of address she had long ago been granted--"don't you want me to think of Apollonie's cottage either?
10142-8{_}3152{_}Shall we have a disappointment, if I hope that we can find a home there?"
10142-8{_}3153{_}"Yes, my dear child.
10142-8{_}3154{_}It is entirely out of the question for you and your brother to live there.
10142-8{_}3155{_}I should not tell you this if I were not absolutely certain, and you can imagine that I should not shatter such a hope if I did not have to."
10142-8{_}3156{_}It hurt Mrs. Maxa very much to say this, but she found it necessary.
10142-8{_}3157{_}She knew that Apollonie in her measureless love and admiration would never be able to refuse a single one of Leonore's wishes, even if it meant the impossible.
10142-8{_}3158{_}"I shall not think about it any more then," said Leonore, embracing Mrs. Maxa with utter confidence, "and I shall be glad now that I can still remain with you."
10142-8{_}3159{_}Later that evening when the children were all together and Leonore had conquered her grief for that day, a letter came for their mother from Hanover.
10142-8{_}3160{_}She had informed the ladies of Leonore's complete recovery and had added that the doctor thought it necessary for the child to enjoy the strengthening mountain air for a while longer.
10142-8{_}3161{_}She herself had no other wish than to keep Leonore in her house as long as possible.
10142-8{_}3162{_}The ladies' answer was full of warm thanks for her great help in their embarrassing situation.
10142-8{_}3163{_}They were very glad to accept her great kindness for two more weeks, after which one of them would come to fetch Leonore home.
10142-8{_}3164{_}Mrs. Maxa glanced with a heavy heart at the child to whom she had grown as devoted as to her own.
10142-8{_}3165{_}She felt dreadfully sad at the thought of letting her go away so soon.
10142-8{_}3166{_}The worst of it was that she knew the ladies' abode had never really meant a home for poor Leonore.
10142-8{_}3167{_}It only doubled her grief to know how hard it would be for the child to leave her, but as she had no right over her, she could do nothing.
10142-8{_}3168{_}The only thing she could plan was to ask the ladies to let her have Leonore sometimes during the summer holidays.
10142-8{_}3169{_}She decided not to dampen the children's good spirits that evening with the discouraging news in the letter.
10142-8{_}3170{_}CHAPTER VIII  MÄZLI PAYS VISITS  Whenever Mäzli found the time heavy on her hands, she would suddenly remember people who might want to see her.
10142-8{_}3171{_}She had been extremely occupied all these days entertaining Leonore, as during school hours she had been the older girl's sole companion.
10142-8{_}3172{_}Her brothers and sisters were now home for a holiday and constantly surrounded Leonore.
10142-8{_}3173{_}Finding herself without her usual employment, Mäzli ran after her mother on the morning of the holiday and kept on saying, "I must go to see Apollonie.
10142-8{_}3174{_}I am sure Loneli is sad that I have not been to see her so long," until her mother finally gave her permission to go that afternoon.
10142-8{_}3175{_}On her way to Apollonie Mäzli had been struck by an idea which occupied her very much.
10142-8{_}3176{_}She arrived at the cottage of her old friend and sat down beside Loneli, who was not in the least sad, but looked about her with the merriest eyes.
10142-8{_}3177{_}"I must go see the Castle-Steward to-day," she said quickly.
10142-8{_}3178{_}"I promised it but I forgot about it."
10142-8{_}3179{_}"No, no, Mäzli," Apollonie said evasively, "we have lots of other things to do.
10142-8{_}3180{_}We have to see if the plums are getting ripe on the tree in the corner of the garden, and after that you must see the chickens.
10142-8{_}3181{_}Just think, Mäzli, they have little chicks, and you will have to see them.
10142-8{_}3182{_}I am sure you won't ever want to leave them."
10142-8{_}3183{_}"Oh, yes, when I have seen them I must go to the Castle-Steward because I promised to," Mäzli replied.
10142-8{_}3184{_}"I am sure he has forgotten all about it and does not remember you any more," Apollonie said, trying to ward Mäzli off from her design.
10142-8{_}3185{_}"Does your mama know that you mean to go to the castle?"
10142-8{_}3186{_}"No, because I only thought of it on my way here," Mäzli assured her old friend.
10142-8{_}3187{_}"But one must always keep a promise; Kurt told me that."
10142-8{_}3188{_}"Mr. Trius won't even let you in," Apollonie protested.
10142-8{_}3189{_}"Certainly!
10142-8{_}3190{_}He has to.

10142-8{_}3342{_}The mother had been very careful in keeping the contents of Miss Remke's letter from the children in order not to spoil their last two weeks together.

10142-8{_}3344{_}Salo remarked quite frankly that he himself hardly looked forward to Leonore's coming, as he saw in each of her letters how happy she was in Aunt Maxa's household and how difficult the separation would be for her.
10142-8{_}3345{_}Whenever he thought how hard it would be for her to grow accustomed to the change again, all his joy vanished at the prospect of her return.
10142-8{_}3346{_}Bruno had read the whole letter aloud and had therewith conjured up such consternation and grief on every side that the mother hardly knew how to comfort them.

10142-8{_}3441{_}"Just come!
10142-8{_}3442{_}Leonore.
10142-8{_}3443{_}Look!
10142-8{_}3444{_}there he sits already."
10142-8{_}3445{_}With this Mäzli flew over to the large pine tree.
10142-8{_}3446{_}"How do you do, Mr. Castle-Steward!
10142-8{_}3447{_}Didn't I come soon again, this time?"
10142-8{_}3448{_}she merrily called out to him.
10142-8{_}3449{_}"I have also brought everything I promised.
10142-8{_}3450{_}Here are the picture books--look!
10142-8{_}3451{_}two of them.
10142-8{_}3452{_}I thought you might look through one too quickly."
10142-8{_}3453{_}Mäzli laid both books on the lion skin and began to rummage through her pockets.
10142-8{_}3454{_}"Look what else I brought you," and Mäzli laid down a tiny ivory whistle.
10142-8{_}3455{_}"Kurt gave it to me once and now I give it to you.
10142-8{_}3456{_}If you have a headache and Mr. Trius is far away, all you need to do is to whistle.
10142-8{_}3457{_}Then he can come and bring you some water.
10142-8{_}3458{_}He'll hear it far, far away, because it whistles as loud as anything.
10142-8{_}3459{_}Just try it once!
10142-8{_}3460{_}I have also brought you Leonore."
10142-8{_}3461{_}The gentleman started slightly and looked up.
10142-8{_}3462{_}Leonore had shyly retreated behind the chair, but Mäzli pulled her forward.
10142-8{_}3463{_}The gentleman now threw a penetrating glance at the delicate looking little girl, who hardly dared to raise her large, dark eyes to his.
10142-8{_}3464{_}Leonore, who had blushed violently under his scrutiny, said in a barely audible voice, "Perhaps we should not have come; but Mäzli thought we might be allowed to see you.
10142-8{_}3465{_}Can we do something for you?
10142-8{_}3466{_}Perhaps Mäzli should not have brought me.
10142-8{_}3467{_}Oh, I am so sorry if I have offended you."
10142-8{_}3468{_}"No, indeed.
10142-8{_}3469{_}Mäzli meant well when she wanted me to meet her friend," the gentleman said in quite a friendly voice.
10142-8{_}3470{_}"What is the name of Mäzli's friend?"
10142-8{_}3471{_}"Leonore von Wallerstätten," the girl answered, and noticing the large books on the gentleman's knees, she added, "May I take the books away?
10142-8{_}3472{_}They might be too heavy."
10142-8{_}3473{_}"Yes, you might, but it was very good of Mäzli to bring them all the way up to me," he said.
10142-8{_}3474{_}"I'll look at them a little later."
10142-8{_}3475{_}"May I fix your pillow for you?
10142-8{_}3476{_}It does not do you much good that way," said Leonore, pulling it up.
10142-8{_}3477{_}It had long ago slipped out of position.
10142-8{_}3478{_}"Oh, this is better, this is lovely," the sick man replied, comfortably leaning back in the chair.
10142-8{_}3479{_}"What a shame!
10142-8{_}3480{_}It won't stay, I am afraid.
10142-8{_}3481{_}It is falling down again," said Leonore regretfully.
10142-8{_}3482{_}"We ought to have a ribbon.
10142-8{_}3483{_}If I only had one and a thread and needle!--but perhaps we could come again to-morrow--"  Leonore became quite frightened suddenly at her boldness and remained silent from embarrassment.
10142-8{_}3484{_}But Mäzli got her out of this trying situation.
10142-8{_}3485{_}Full of confidence she announced that they would return the next day with everything necessary.
10142-8{_}3486{_}The gentleman now asked Leonore where she came from and where she lived.
10142-8{_}3487{_}She related that she had been living in a boarding school for several years, ever since the death of her great-aunt, with whom both she and her brother had found a home.
10142-8{_}3488{_}"Have you no other relations?"
10142-8{_}3489{_}the gentleman asked, keenly observing her the while.
10142-8{_}3490{_}"No, none at all, except an uncle who has been living in Spain for many years.
10142-8{_}3491{_}My aunt told us that he won't ever come back and that no one knows where he is.
10142-8{_}3492{_}If we knew where he is, we should have written to him long ago.
10142-8{_}3493{_}Salo would go to Spain as soon as he was allowed to and I should go to him in any case."
10142-8{_}3494{_}"Why?"
10142-8{_}3495{_}the gentleman asked.
10142-8{_}3496{_}"Because he is our father's brother," she replied, "and we could love him like a father, too.
10142-8{_}3497{_}He is the only person in the whole world to whom we could belong.
10142-8{_}3498{_}We have wished many and many a time a chance to look for him, because we might live with him."
10142-8{_}3499{_}"No, you couldn't do that.
10142-8{_}3500{_}I know him, I have been in Spain," the Castle-Steward said curtly.
10142-8{_}3501{_}A light spread over Leonore's face, as if her heart had been suddenly flooded with hope.
10142-8{_}3502{_}"Oh, do you really know our uncle?
10142-8{_}3503{_}Do you know where he is living?"
10142-8{_}3504{_}she cried out, while her cheeks flushed with happiness.
10142-8{_}3505{_}"Oh, please tell me what you know about him."
10142-8{_}3506{_}When she gazed up at the gentleman with such sparkling eyes, it seemed to him that he ought to consider his reply carefully.
10142-8{_}3507{_}Suddenly he said positively, "No, no, you can never seek him out.
10142-8{_}3508{_}Your uncle is an old, sick man, and no young people could possibly live with him.
10142-8{_}3509{_}He must remain alone in his old owl's nest.
10142-8{_}3510{_}You could not go to him there."
10142-8{_}3511{_}"But we should go to him so much more, if he is old and ill.
10142-8{_}3512{_}He needs us more then than if he had a family," Leonore said eagerly.
10142-8{_}3513{_}"He could be our father and we his children and we could take care of him and love him.
10142-8{_}3514{_}If he only were not so dreadfully far away!
10142-8{_}3515{_}If you could only tell us where he lives, we could write to him and get his permission to go there.
10142-8{_}3516{_}Without him we can't do anything at all, because Mr. von Stiele in Hanover wants Salo to study for years and years longer.
10142-8{_}3517{_}We have to do everything he says, unless our uncle should call us.
10142-8{_}3518{_}Oh, please tell me where he lives!"
10142-8{_}3519{_}"Just think of all the deprivations you would have to suffer with your old uncle!
10142-8{_}3520{_}Think how lonely it would be for you to live with a sick man in a wild nest among the rocks!
10142-8{_}3521{_}What do you say to that?"
10142-8{_}3522{_}he said curtly.
10142-8{_}3523{_}"Oh, it would only be glorious for Salo and me to have a real home with an uncle we loved," Leonore continued, showing that her longing could not be quenched.
10142-8{_}3524{_}"There is only one thing I should miss there, but I have to miss it in Hanover, too.
10142-8{_}3525{_}I shall never, never feel at home there!"
10142-8{_}3526{_}"Well, what is this?"
10142-8{_}3527{_}the gentleman queried.
10142-8{_}3528{_}"That I can't be together with Aunt Maxa and the children."
10142-8{_}3529{_}"Shall we ask Aunt Maxa's advice?
10142-8{_}3530{_}Would this suit you, child?"
10142-8{_}3531{_}"Oh, yes indeed," Leonore answered happily.
10142-8{_}3532{_}At the mention of Aunt Maxa she suddenly remembered that they had not told her where they were going.
10142-8{_}3533{_}As she was afraid that they had remained away too long already, Lenore urged Mäzli to take her leave quickly, while she gave her hand to the steward.
10142-8{_}3534{_}"Will you deliver a message for me, Leonore?"
10142-8{_}3535{_}he said; "will you tell your Aunt Maxa that the master of the castle, whom she knew long years ago, would love to visit her, but he is unable?
10142-8{_}3536{_}Ask her if he may hope that she will come up to him at the castle instead?"
10142-8{_}3537{_}Mäzli gave her hand now to say good-bye, and when she noticed that the pillow had slipped down again, she said, "Apollonie would just love to set things in order for you, but Mr. Trius won't let her in.
10142-8{_}3538{_}She would be willing to give a finger from her right hand if she were allowed to do everything Mr. Trius doesn't do."
10142-8{_}3539{_}"Come now, Mäzli," said Leonore, for she had the feeling that this peculiar revelation might be followed by others as unintelligible.
10142-8{_}3540{_}But the Castle-Steward smiled, as if he had comprehended Mäzli's words.
10142-8{_}3541{_}Mrs. Maxa was standing in front of her house, surrounded by her children, anxiously looking for the two missing ones.
10142-8{_}3542{_}Nobody could understand where Leonore and Mäzli might have stayed so long.
10142-8{_}3543{_}Suddenly they caught a glimpse of two blue ribbons fluttering from Leonore's hat.
10142-8{_}3544{_}Quickly the children rushed to meet them.
10142-8{_}3545{_}"Where do you come from?
10142-8{_}3546{_}Where did you stay so long?
10142-8{_}3547{_}Where have you been all this time," sounded from all sides.
10142-8{_}3548{_}"In the castle," was the answer.
10142-8{_}3549{_}The excitement only grew at this.
10142-8{_}3550{_}"How could you get there?
10142-8{_}3551{_}Who opened the door?
10142-8{_}3552{_}What did you do at the castle?"
10142-8{_}3553{_}The questions were poured out at such a rate that no answer could possibly have been heard.
10142-8{_}3554{_}"I went to see the Castle-Steward before.
10142-8{_}3555{_}I have been to see him quite often," said Mäzli loudly, for she was desirous of being heard.
10142-8{_}3556{_}Leonore had gone ahead with the mother's arm linked in hers, for she was very anxious to deliver her message.
10142-8{_}3557{_}Kurt was too much interested in Mäzli's expedition to the castle to be frightened off by the first unintelligible account.
10142-8{_}3558{_}He had to find out how it had come about and what had happened, but the two did not get very far in their dialogue.
10142-8{_}3559{_}As soon as Mäzli began to talk first about Mr. Trius and then about the Steward, Kurt always said quickly, "But this is all one and the same person.
10142-8{_}3560{_}Don't make two out of them, Mäzli!
10142-8{_}3561{_}All the world knows that Mr. Trius is the Steward of Castle Wildenstein; he is one person and not two."
10142-8{_}3562{_}Then Mäzli answered, "Mr. Trius is one and the Castle-Steward is another.
10142-8{_}3563{_}They are two people and not one."
10142-8{_}3564{_}After they had repeated this about three times Bruno said, "Oh, Kurt, leave her alone.
10142-8{_}3565{_}Mäzli thinks that there are two, when she calls him first Mr. Trius and then Mr.
10142-8{_}3566{_}Castle-Steward."
10142-8{_}3567{_}That was too much for Mäzli, and shouting vigorously, "They are two people, they are two people," she ran away.
10142-8{_}3568{_}Leonore had related in the meantime how Mäzli had proposed to visit the sick Castle-Steward and how she had at first been reluctant to go, till Mäzli had made her feel that she was wrong.
10142-8{_}3569{_}She related everything that had happened and all the questions he had asked her.
10142-8{_}3570{_}"Just think, Aunt Maxa," Leonore went on, "the gentleman knows our uncle in Spain.
10142-8{_}3571{_}He said that he had been there, too, and he knows that our uncle is old and ill and is living all by himself.
10142-8{_}3572{_}I wanted so much to find out where he was, and asked him to tell me, but he thought it would not help, as we couldn't possibly go to him.
10142-8{_}3573{_}So I said that we might write, and just think, Aunt Maxa!
10142-8{_}3574{_}at last he said he would ask your advice."
10142-8{_}3575{_}Then Leonore gave her message.
10142-8{_}3576{_}"He did not say that the Castle-Steward, as he called himself to Mäzli, sent the message, but told me that it was from the master of the castle, whom you knew a long time ago," Leonore concluded.
10142-8{_}3577{_}"Oh, just think!
10142-8{_}3578{_}Aunt Maxa, we might find our uncle after all.
10142-8{_}3579{_}Oh, please help us, for I want so much to write to him."
10142-8{_}3580{_}Mrs. Maxa had listened with ever-growing agitation, and she was so deeply affected that she could not say a word.
10142-8{_}3581{_}She could not express the thought which thrilled her so, because she did not know the Baron's intentions.
10142-8{_}3582{_}Mea's loud complaints at this moment conveniently hid her mother's silence.
10142-8{_}3583{_}"Oh, Leonore," she cried out, "if you go to Spain, we shan't see each other again for the rest of our lives; then you will never, never come back here any more!"
10142-8{_}3584{_}"Do you really think so?"
10142-8{_}3585{_}Leonore asked, much downcast.
10142-8{_}3586{_}She felt that it would be hard for her to choose in such a case, and she suddenly did not know if she really wanted to go to Spain.
10142-8{_}3587{_}"It is not very easy to make a trip to Spain, children," said the mother, "and I am sure that it is not necessary to get excited about it."
10142-8{_}3588{_}When Kurt, after the belated supper that night, renewed his examination about the single or the double Steward of Castle Wildenstein, their mother announced that bedtime had not only come for the little ones, but for all.
10142-8{_}3589{_}Soon after, the whole lively party was sleeping soundly and only the mother was still sitting in her room, sunk in deep meditation.
10142-8{_}3590{_}She had not been able to think over the Baron's words till now and she wondered what hopes she might build upon them.
10142-8{_}3591{_}He might only want to talk over Leonore's situation because he had realized how little she felt at home in Hanover.
10142-8{_}3592{_}But all this thinking led to nothing, and she knew that our good Lord in heaven, who opens doors which seem most tightly barred, had let it happen for a purpose.
10142-8{_}3593{_}She was so grateful that she would be able to see the person who, more than anyone else, held Leonore's destiny in his hands.
10142-8{_}3594{_}Full of confidence in God, she hoped that the hand which had opened an impassable road would also lead an embittered heart back to himself, and by renewing in him the love of his fellowmen, bring about much happiness and joy.
10142-8{_}3595{_}CHAPTER IX  IN THE CASTLE  The next afternoon, after planning a pleasant walk for Leonore and Mäzli, Mrs. Maxa started on her way to the castle.
10142-8{_}3596{_}As soon as she neared the grated iron door it opened wide, and holding his hat in his hand, Mr. Trius stood deeply bowing in the opening.
10142-8{_}3597{_}"May I see the Baron?"
10142-8{_}3598{_}asked Mrs. Maxa.
10142-8{_}3599{_}After another reverence Mr. Trius led the visitor up the hill, and when he had duly announced her, invited her with a third bow to step forward.
10142-8{_}3600{_}It was quite evident that Mr. Trius had been definitely ordered to change his usual mode of behaviour.
10142-8{_}3601{_}Mrs. Maxa now approached the chair near the pine tree.
10142-8{_}3602{_}"Have you really come, Mrs.
10142-8{_}3603{_}Maxa?"
10142-8{_}3604{_}said the sick man, putting out his hand.
10142-8{_}3605{_}"Did no bitter feelings against the evil-doer keep you back?"
10142-8{_}3606{_}Mrs. Maxa pressed the proffered hand and replied, "I could wish for no greater joy, Baron, than to have your door opened for me.
10142-8{_}3607{_}I have wondered oftener than you could think if this would ever happen, for I wanted an opportunity to serve you.
10142-8{_}3608{_}I know no bitter feelings and never have known them.
10142-8{_}3609{_}Everybody who has loved this castle and its inmates has known they suffered grief and pain."
10142-8{_}3610{_}"I returned to this old cave here to die," said the Baron.
10142-8{_}3611{_}"You can see plainly that I am a broken man.
10142-8{_}3612{_}I only wished to forget the past in this solitude, and I thought it right for me to die forgotten.
10142-8{_}3613{_}Then your little girl came in here one day--I have not been able to discover how."
10142-8{_}3614{_}"Oh, please forgive her," said Mrs. Maxa.
10142-8{_}3615{_}"It is a riddle to me, too, how she succeeded in entering this garden.
10142-8{_}3616{_}I knew nothing about it till yesterday evening when the children came home from the castle.
10142-8{_}3617{_}I am terribly afraid that Mäzli has annoyed you."
10142-8{_}3618{_}"She has not done so at all, for she is her mother's true child," said the Baron.
10142-8{_}3619{_}"She was so anxious to help me and to bring me what I lacked.
10142-8{_}3620{_}Because she loved Leonore so much, she wanted me to know her, too, but I cannot understand Leonore.
10142-8{_}3621{_}She begged and begged to be allowed to see her uncle, as she wished to live with him and love him like a father.
10142-8{_}3622{_}She even longs to seek him out in a foreign country.
10142-8{_}3623{_}What shall I do?
10142-8{_}3624{_}Please give me your advice, Mrs.
10142-8{_}3625{_}Maxa."
10142-8{_}3626{_}"There is only one thing to do, Baron," the lady replied with an overflowing heart.
10142-8{_}3627{_}"God Himself has done what we never could have accomplished, despite all our wishes.
10142-8{_}3628{_}The child has been led into your arms by God and therefore belongs to you from now on.
10142-8{_}3629{_}You must become her father and let her love and take care of you.
10142-8{_}3630{_}You will soon realize what a treasure she is, and through her the good old times will come back to this castle.
10142-8{_}3631{_}You will grow young again yourself as soon as you two are here together."
10142-8{_}3632{_}The Baron replied: "Our dear Maxa always saw things in an ideal light.
10142-8{_}3633{_}How could a delicate child like Leonore fit into a wilderness like this castle.
10142-8{_}3634{_}Everything here is deserted and forlorn.
10142-8{_}3635{_}Just think of the old watchman here and me, what miserable housemates we should be.
10142-8{_}3636{_}Won't you receive the child in your house, for she clearly longs to have a home?
10142-8{_}3637{_}I know that she will find one there and apparently has found it already.
10142-8{_}3638{_}She can learn by and by who her uncle is and then she can come to visit him sometimes."
10142-8{_}3639{_}Amazed at this sudden change, Mrs. Maxa was silent for a while.
10142-8{_}3640{_}How she would have rejoiced at this prospect a few days ago!
10142-8{_}3641{_}"I love Leonore like my own child and wanted nothing better than to keep her with me," she said finally, "but I think differently now.
10142-8{_}3642{_}The children belong to you, and the castle of their fathers must become their home.
10142-8{_}3643{_}You must let Leonore surround you with her delightful and soothing personality, which is sure to make you happy.
10142-8{_}3644{_}When you come to know her you will soon realize of what I should have robbed you.
10142-8{_}3645{_}There is no necessity at all for the castle to remain forlorn and empty.
10142-8{_}3646{_}Despite the loss of our dear loved ones, the life here can again become as pleasant as in former times.
10142-8{_}3647{_}Your mother always hoped that this would happen at her eldest son's return, as she had desired that his home should remain unchanged even after her death.
10142-8{_}3648{_}Leonore can have her quarters in your mother's rooms."
10142-8{_}3649{_}"I wonder if you would like to see the rooms you knew so well, Mrs. Maxa," the Baron said slowly.
10142-8{_}3650{_}Mrs. Maxa gladly assented to this.
10142-8{_}3651{_}"May I go everywhere?"
10142-8{_}3652{_}she asked.
10142-8{_}3653{_}"I know my way so well."
10142-8{_}3654{_}"Certainly, wherever you wish," the Baron replied.
10142-8{_}3655{_}Entering the large hall, Mrs. Maxa was filled with deep emotion.
10142-8{_}3656{_}Here she had spent the most beautiful days of her childhood in delicious games with the unforgettable Leonore and the two young Barons.
10142-8{_}3657{_}Everything was as it had been then.
10142-8{_}3658{_}The large stone table in the middle, the stone benches on the walls and the niches with the old knights of Wallerstätten stood there as of yore.
10142-8{_}3659{_}When she went into the dining-hall, everything looked bare and empty.
10142-8{_}3660{_}The portraits of ancestors had been taken from the walls and the glinting pewter plates and goblets were gone from the large oaken sideboard.
10142-8{_}3661{_}Mrs. Maxa shook her head.
10142-8{_}3662{_}Going up the stairs, she decided first of all to go to the Baron's rooms, for she wondered what care he was receiving.
10142-8{_}3663{_}Rigid with consternation, she stopped under the doorway.
10142-8{_}3664{_}What a room it was!
10142-8{_}3665{_}Not the tiniest picture was on the wall and not a single small rug lay on the uneven boards.
10142-8{_}3666{_}Nothing but an empty bedstead, an old wicker chair and a table which had plainly been dragged there from the servants' quarters, comprised the furniture.
10142-8{_}3667{_}Mrs. Maxa looked again to make sure that it was really the Baron's room.
10142-8{_}3668{_}There was no doubt of it, it was the balcony room in the tower.
10142-8{_}3669{_}Where did the Baron sleep?
10142-8{_}3670{_}As the sight proved more than she could bear, she quickly sought the late Baroness' chamber.
10142-8{_}3671{_}Here, too, everything was empty and the red plush-covered chairs and the sofa in the corner over which all the pictures of the children used to hang were gone.
10142-8{_}3672{_}Only an empty bedstead stood in the corner.
10142-8{_}3673{_}Mrs. Maxa went next to Leonore's room, which used to be extremely pretty.
10142-8{_}3674{_}Lovely pictures used to hang on the walls, chairs covered in light blue silk were standing about, a half-rounded bed was placed in a corner, and she remembered the dearest little desk on which two flower vases, always filled with fresh roses, used to stand.
10142-8{_}3675{_}Mrs. Maxa did not even go in this time, it was too horribly forlorn.
10142-8{_}3676{_}The only thing which still spoke of old times was the wallpaper with the tiny red and blue flowers.
10142-8{_}3677{_}She quickly went out.
10142-8{_}3678{_}Throwing a single glance at the large ball-room, she likened it to a dreary desert.
10142-8{_}3679{_}Not a curtain, not a chair or painting could be seen.
10142-8{_}3680{_}Where could all the valuable damask-covered furniture have gone to?
10142-8{_}3681{_}Was it possible that the castle had been robbed and no one knew of it?
10142-8{_}3682{_}It was probable, however, that Mr. Trius did not know about anything, and it was plain that the Baron himself had not troubled about these things.
10142-8{_}3683{_}Mrs. Maxa hurriedly went back to him.
10142-8{_}3684{_}"To what a dreary home you have come back, my poor friend!"
10142-8{_}3685{_}she cried out, "and I know that your mother never wished you to find it like this.
10142-8{_}3686{_}How unhappy you must have felt when you entered these walls after so many years!
10142-8{_}3687{_}You cannot help feeling miserable here, and it is all quite incomprehensible to me."
10142-8{_}3688{_}"Not to me," the Baron quietly replied; "I somehow felt it had to be that way.
10142-8{_}3689{_}Did I value my home before?
10142-8{_}3690{_}It is a just retribution to me to find the place so empty and forlorn.
10142-8{_}3691{_}I only returned to die here and I can await death in daytime on my chair out here and at night time in my nest.
10142-8{_}3692{_}I need nothing further; but death has not come as quickly as I thought it would.
10142-8{_}3693{_}Why are you trying to bring me back to life again?"
10142-8{_}3694{_}"This is what I decidedly mean to do, so we shall banish the subject of death from now on, as I confidently believe that our Lord in Heaven has other plans for you," Mrs. Maxa said decisively.
10142-8{_}3695{_}"I can see for myself that it is better for Leonore to stay with us, and I am ever so happy for your permission.
10142-8{_}3696{_}May I write the ladies in Hanover that you do not want Leonore to be fetched away for the present?"
10142-8{_}3697{_}The Baron heartily gave this permission.
10142-8{_}3698{_}"I have to trouble you for one thing, Baron.

10142-8{_}3700{_}The Baron smilingly answered, "Of course I remember her.

10142-8{_}3709{_}"I do," the Baron replied smilingly, "and I feel that I ought to be obedient."

10142-8{_}3712{_}She had always believed that the Baron would find it home-like and furnished, and now everything was gone, and he had not even a bed to sleep in, but was obliged to spend both day and night in his chair.

10142-8{_}3728{_}But her dreams were not to come true.

10142-8{_}3745{_}Mr. Trius appeared, quietly opened and silently walked away again.
10142-8{_}3746{_}Apollonie, who knew from Mäzli where the master was, went towards the terrace.

10142-8{_}3828{_}Loneli had just heard the great news, because she had been asleep when her grandmother returned the night before.
